# CHAPTER 1 GENERAL

## 1.1 GENERAL PROVISIONS

1.1.1 GENERAL

It is the intent of this Specification and accompanying plan(s) to describe and set forth the design, performance, capacities, construction, equipment and material required for the construction of a Container Vessel (hereinafter called the “Vessel”).

Following accompanying plan(s) shall form an integral part of this Specification:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | General Arrangement Plan | Drawing No. HP4102-100-04 |
|  | Midship Section Plan | Drawing No. HP4102-110-03 |
|  | Maker's List No.GW4001-014-03 | Drawing No. HP4102-014-03 |

This Specification with above mentioned accompanying plans shall form an integral part of the Building Contract of the Vessel.

Details in design, construction, installation, inspection, test and workmanship not covered by this Specification and the accompanying plan(s) shall be performed under the working plans and Builder’s practice. **List of Builder’s standards and practices to be submitted to the Buyer for reference at the time of plan approval.**

The Builder shall furnish the Vessel with all items required by the Rules and Regulations as specified in section 3.3 “Rules and Regulations” and 3.4 “Guidelines and Recommendations”, except items specifically stated herein as shall be furnished and supplied by the Buyer.

Any items repeated by mentioning twice or more in this Specification shall be supplied and/or applied only once. Any items, which are not called for explicitly in this Specification, shall not be furnished nor supplied by the Builder. Any items missing but required by Classification Society or Regulatory Bodies concerned which set force at the date of Contract signing, shall be supplied and/or equipped by the Builder.

Any requirement of the Buyer, which is in excess of the requirements of Rules and Regulations as specified in Section 3.3 “Rules and Regulations” and 3.4 “Guidelines and Recommendations” and/or the content of this Specification, shall be subject to the adjustment to the Contract price, scheduled delivery date, contract speed, deadweight, homogeneous intake and any other items which may be affected.

If any inconsistency is found between the Building Contract and this Specification and/or this Specification and accompanying plans, the former shall prevail in any case.

The description in CHAPTER 1 “General” shall be applied to all parts of this Specification, whereas in the other parts the descriptions shall be applied the respective parts, if not stated otherwise. In the event of any conflict or inconsistency between the parts of this Specification, the hull part shall prevail in respect of hull items, the outfitting part shall prevail in respect of outfitting items, the machinery part shall prevail in respect of machinery items and the electrical part shall prevail in respect of electrical items.

In the event of any inconsistency between the description in the Specification and Rules and/or Regulations listed in the Specification, Rules and/or Regulations shall prevail.

If during approval of plans, both parties agree to a design which differs from the Specification, it is understood that terms in the Specification concerning these alterations shall be no longer applicable, and consequently in these cases the approved drawings shall be supplementary to the Specification.

Any alterations of Rules and Regulations as specified in Part 1, Section 3.3 and Section 3.4 of this Specification coming into effect between the date of Contract signing and ship’s delivery may be carried out subject to adjustment to the Contract price, Contract guaranteed technical data (Speed, Deadweight, Homogeneous intake, etc.), delivery date and any other item(s) which may be affected.

Any amendments and/or modifications in this Specification and/or Contract Plan(s) to be treated similar to above.

If the Buyer desires to apply the said amendment and/or modification to the Vessel, the Buyer will inform the Builder in written document, and the Builder shall submit a written document about their effect on the Vessel's Contract price, Contract guaranteed technical data (Speed, Deadweight, Homogeneous intake, etc.), delivery date and any other item(s), which may affect the Contract.

The amendments and/or modifications shall come into effect after agreement has been reached between the Buyer and the Builder and a written consent has been signed between both parties.

Amendments and/or modifications shall be recorded in a memorandum or a written document signed by the Buyer and the Builder. These documents shall be a supplement to the Contract Specification.

Whenever the terms "or equal" or “or equivalent” is used after a brand or a type of machinery equipment or component, the term "or equal" or “or equivalent” means that the substitute shall be of equivalent standard and quality and should not affect the contracted performance or compliance of the revised system. The Buyer must agree to such a change.

Wherever the terms such as “or”, “and/or”, “similar”, “where necessary”, “if any”, “may” and other similar expressions are mentioned in this Specification, application of alternative item(s) shall be respected to opinion of the Builder. **And the result will be**

**informed to owner.**

Unless otherwise stipulated by the Contract and/or specifically described in this Specification, all figures stated in this Specification shall be understood as approximate ones and determined in accordance with the design development except those which are of countable nature.

Spare Parts, tools and accessories shall be furnished as per rules of Classification Society and Regulatory Bodies concerned and in accordance with the Makers’ normal standard or as listed throughout these Specifications. Any additional spares required by the Buyer shall be supplied by the Builder on the Buyer’s account unless otherwise agreed or stated herein.

Spare parts, Tools and accessories shall be properly protected and stored in a way which guides easy access and control depending on its type and size. However, heavy components of main engine to be arranged under overhead crane working range**.** Steel cabinets, shelves and drawers shall be used for storing spare parts in accordance with the Builder’s practice and recommendations of the Makers.

During the tests and trials, the Builder may use some of the supplied spare parts, tools and accessories to the Vessel if necessary subject to Buyer’s approval, and the Builder shall furnish them back to the Vessel upon ship’s delivery **if deemed critical by Buyers*.***

The Builder may make changes and improvements to the Specification, if found necessary in good condition, provided that the Builder shall first obtain the Buyer's approval which shall not be unreasonably withheld.

1.1.2 design AMBIENT TEMPERATURE

If not otherwise stated, the equipment and machinery to be installed and operated in accordance with following ambient conditions:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Outside air temperature | –19oC ~ + 35oC | |
| Sea Water temperature | 0oC ~ + 32oC | |
| Reference conditions for machinery equipment: | Max. air temperature in engine room: + 45oC  L.T. cooling F.W. temperature: + 36oC  Barometric pressure: 0.1 MPa  Relative humidity: 60% | |
| Reference condition for HVAC – plant for accommodation: | Summer cycle  Outside atmosphere:  Inside atmosphere:  Winter cycle  Outside atmosphere:  Inside atmosphere: | +35oC;70% R.H.  +27oC; 50% R.H.  –20oC; 50% R.H.  +20oC; 50% R.H. |

Note:

1.R.H.: Relative humidity

2. For the materials of hull steel of structures exposed to low air temperatures shall be based on the design temperature tD (the lowest mean daily average air temperature in the area of operation) of -10℃. (refer to IACS UR S6) ***(Rev 9 July 2018)***

1.1.3 MATERIAL AND WORKMANSHIP

Materials supplied and used for construction of the Vessel shall be of such quality as approved by the Classification Society where required.

Ordering of materials, machinery and equipment shall comply with this Specification and Maker List.

**All structural steel used for the construction of the vessel including forgings and castings to be of the shipbuilding and marine engineering quality, tested, inspected and certified as required by the Classification Society. In addition, steel plates certificates to be provided to the Site Team before inspection *by group.******the first group will submit before steel cut.***

For any materials, machinery and equipment specified in the Maker List, selection of the

final Makers shall be as per the signed Maker List.. For other materials, machinery and equipment not specified in the Maker List, the Builder shall have the right to decide the Maker and/or supplier according to Builder’s own knowledge and experience.

Manufacturer’s standard type, size and material of machinery, equipment and fittings shall be adopted unless otherwise described in this Specification.

The manufacturer or Maker of equipment has the right to improve or update the production after the contract has been made between the Maker and the Builder which shall not be unreasonably withheld by the Buyer.

The Builder may employ sub-contractors for carrying out works of the Vessel at the

Builder’s responsibility and the Builder shall guarantee the work / quality of subcontractors.

If any materials and equipment described in this Specification is not available, the Builder shall substitute equivalent materials and equipment capable of satisfying the

requirements of Classification Society and relevant Regulations and subject to prior

acceptance of the Buyer.

If any of the specific description for the machinery or equipment in this Specification is not consistent with the finally selected manufacturer’s specifications, such description shall be readily corrected to follow the manufacturer’s specification.

Wherever stainless steel is mentioned in the specifications and unless otherwise specified,

this means quality of SUS304, or corresponding Maker’s standard may be applied. **However, SS 301 shall not be used. In case of maker standard, quality shall be SUS 304 *or above*.**

Workmanship shall be carried out in accordance with the descriptions in this Specification, China Shipbuilding Quality Standard (CSQS) (GB/T34000-2016) and Builder's Engineering Standard.

Asbestos, Refrigerant (R 12 / R 22), HALON, Lead-based paint and Tin-based antifouling paint shall not be used.

All wood to be well seasoned and free from defect.

1.1.4 STANDARD

The following standards shall be applied to the construction of the Vessel.

1) Chinese Industrial Standard (GB, GB/T, YB)

2) Chinese Shipbuilding Standard (CB, CB/T, CBM)

3) China Shipbuilding Quality Standard (CSQS)(GB/T34000-2016)

4) Builder's Engineering Standard and Builder's standard practice or Manufacturer’s standards unless otherwise described in the Specification.

5) ISO standard

6) IACS Rec.47 Shipbuilding and Repair Quality Standard(Part A)

7) JIS or DIN standard

The connection dimension of flange shall be in accordance with ISO standard except those flange attached on the imported equipment, which shall be as per Maker's standard.

The grease nipples shall be of flat type (CB/T 3762-1996 eqv ISO7824-1986, Material: brass) or the Maker's standard which is provided by the equipment supplier as a package.

In addition to above, other standards may be applied for the items or equipment which is described hereinafter in this Specification except those grease nipples attached on the imported equipment, which will be as per Maker's standard.

1.1.5 MEASUREMENT UNIT AND LANGUAGE

Metric system shall be adopted for design and construction of hull, machinery and equipment unless specially specified in the Specification.

All measuring units such as power, pressure gauge, thermometer, volume gauge, and tank scales, etc., shall be of metric system. However, some conventional units are also to substitute the corresponding SI units or metric units as common customs in shipbuilding and shipping metric threads to be generally applied to the Vessel, however, the British measurement also may be applied where ISO is not adopted. For pressure, MPa or bar shall be used throughout**.**

Types, sizes and materials of fittings, equipment and machinery to be in accordance with ISO or equivalent standard. Where no applicable ISO or national standard exists, the Builder's standard and/or Manufacturer's standard may be used.

The draught of the Vessel specified in this Specification shall be of moulded figure unless specifically stated.

All necessary documents and drawings, calculations, instruction manuals, etc. to be written in English or in both English and other language (English part shall prevail) for approval by the Buyer, Classification Society and Authorities. All final plans and drawings shall be in English or in both English and other language.

All plans, booklets, name plates, caution/identification plates and whatever documents required for implementation of the Specification shall be in English.

If any language other than English is required by any reason whatever, the text of translation shall be provided by the Buyer.

1.1.6 BUYER'S SUPPLY

Following items including their accessories and spares to be furnished and supplied by the Buyer at Buyer’s own expense, and installed on the Vessel by the Builder, at the time designated by the Builder to meet the Builder’s construction schedule of the Vessel.

The Buyer shall furnish the necessary specifications, plans instruction books, manuals, test reports, test certificates and the manufacturer’s service engineer(s) etc. of the listed items as required by the Builder, which shall form an integral part of the Buyer’s supplies.

The supervision fees related to final commissioning, inspection and certifications of the Buyer’s supply items shall be paid by the Buyer. The Buyer shall be responsible for the adjustment, inspection and certifications of the Buyer’s supply items with Builder’s assistance.

The Builder shall be responsible for storing and handling of Owner's supply items after delivery to the Builder's yard and shall store those items in the Vessel.

The Buyer’s supply items shall be as follows:

1. Charts in general and all nautical books (nautical almanacs, international signal books, ITU books, register tide table, etc.).
2. Electronic charts for ECDIS.
3. Flags, signals and nautical instruments in excess of those specified in the Specification.
4. Hobby equipment such as T.V, broadcasting video, etc. in excess of those specified in Specification.
5. Steel wire, mooring ropes, towing rope and ETA fittings in excess of ***Class Rules and Flag Authority and those specified in*** the Building Specification.
6. Personal computers and printers with peripheral devices for computer network system. Computer network cables and sockets to be provided by Builder.
7. Painting and pictures including frames and other decorations. (Builder to frame and position).
8. Suez Canal searchlight excluding bridge wing search light (the foundation, power socket and manual operated davit for Suez Canal search light shall be installed by the Builder).
9. All office machine including copy machine, fax machine and stationery including pencils, rulers, papers, etc.
10. All gymnastic apparatus.
11. All medicine and medical equipment.
12. Galley and pantry utensils including pans, cutlery, crockery, and glassware.
13. Linen including blanket, carpets, bed sheets, pillows, towels and table cloth, etc.
14. Bedding except mattresses.
15. Brooms, brushes, vacuum cleaners, and waste baskets, etc. for accommodation and all portable hoses and clean devices not mentioned in the Specification.
16. Boatswain’s and carpenter’s tools and inventory other than those specified in the Specification.
17. Fuel oil (HFO,LSHFO / ULSFO/MGO) for actual service after delivery at Builder yard.
18. Lubrication oil, greases and operating oils of all machinery and equipment for actual service after ship’s delivery at Builder’s shipyard. However lubrication oil, greases and operating oils shall be purchased by the Buyer on behalf of the Builder prior to the tests and trials, and the Builder shall calculate and pay back the cost based on the quantity consumed during the tests and trials in accordance with the Contract.
19. Consumable stores including sanitary and all chandlery (soap, etc.).
20. Boiler feed water test kit and chemical compounds for the treatment of feed water and cooling fresh water. And test kit for fuel oil and lubrication oil, hydraulic oil.
21. Cable for power feeding circuits between reefer container and receptacle.
22. Container loose fittings
23. Container spreader, if necessary.
24. Garbage compactor.
25. Cable for electrical power shore connection.
26. Test kit for Class notation on shaft condition monitoring.
27. Portable atmosphere testing instrument for measuring concentration of oxygen, flammable gases or vapors, hydrogen sulphide and carbon monoxide.
28. Portable toilet, potable water, cable and antenna of the Iridium radio for the anti-piracy citadel.
29. Fire ropes for Suez Canal
30. Ship’s local area network
31. All hoses, etc., other than those required by the Rules, or mentioned in these specifications.
32. All other spares, store and equipment in excess of Rule guidelines, Maker’s standard and those listed in the Specification.
33. VSAT equipment (Builder to install).

The Buyer to supply following documents approved by Classification Society with the Builder’s assistance:

1. Training Manual
2. Fire fighting fixed and portable system manual and maintenance manual, and train manual
3. -Garbage Management Plan and Garbage Record Book
4. - Safety Management Certificate (SMC) and Document of Compliance (DOC) for deck, engine and cabin stores supplied by the Buyer.
5. - Minimum Safe Manning Document
6. - Container Securing Manual(CSM)
7. Ship Energy Efficiency Management Plan (SEEMP) (Builder to assist Buyer with necessary plans)
8. International Ship Security Certificate (ISSC) and Ship Security Plan (SSP) covering the requirement of ISPS Code except Automatic Identification System (AIS), ship security alert System (SSAS) and Ship’s Identification number (IMO number)
9. - Fuel Oil Changeover Procedure and Logbook
10. - Ship-specific Plans and Procedures Recovery Persons from the Water
11. - Pilot Card
12. - Maneuvering Booklet
13. - Muster List

Emergency Towing Procedure and Maneuvering Booklet, Shipboard Oil Pollution Emergency Plan (SOPEP), Inventory of Hazardous Materials (IHM) to be provided by builder with Buyer’s assistance. The buyer provided a sample.

## 1.2 DESCRIPTION OF THE VESSEL

1.2.1 GENERAL ARRANGEMENT

The Vessel to be designed and constructed as a full cellular container carrier for unrestricted world-wide ocean going service (except NOx ECA Tier III area and other areas which are stated or limited by the rules and regulation in section 1.3.3, the design and equipment condition of the specification), suitable for carrying dry cargo containers, reefer containers and specified dangerous cargo in closed containers within the scope of the Specification.

The vessel to be an ocean-going gearless container vessel with a single-acting two stroke turbo charged diesel engine, a fixed pitch propeller and a semi-spade rudder. .

The vessel is not service for NOx ECA (Tier III) area and do not comply with the rules and regulations regarding NOx Tier III. The vessel shall be built on the basis of Tier II regulation with the certificate of International Air Pollution Protection Certificate (IAPP) and Statement of compliance with the NOx technical code for main & aux. engine (EIAPP) in compliance with Tier II criterion.

**Open loop scrubber to be provided to satisfy the requirements of Global Sulfur Cap 2020 (option requirement of SECA).**

**HFO (< 3.5% Sulphur), LSHFO (< 0.5% Sulphur)/ULSFO (< 0.1% Sulphur) and MGO(< 0.1% Sulphur) to be loaded on board.**

**ULSFO (< 0.1% Sulphur), MGO (< 0.1% Sulphur) shall be adopted for on SOx Emission Control Area (SECA).**

The vessel to have a continuous main deck with a detached forecastle, eight (8) tiers of deck house.

The propulsion machinery and living quarters including navigation bridge shall be located semi-aft as shown on the General Arrangement Plan (hereinafter called as the "G.A. plan").

Containers, cargo holds, ballast water tanks, fuel oil tanks, fresh water tanks, bow thruster room, steering gear room and engine room etc. shall be arranged as shown on the G.A. plan.

The Vessel shall have four (4) cargo holds. each cargo hold have two (2) hatches each.

The double hull and double bottom space shall be arranged as ballast water tanks or void space. Fore peak tank shall be designed as ballast tank. Aft peak tank shall be designed asballast tank. One pair of anti-heeling tanks to be arranged at midship area port and starboard sides as shown on GA plan.

Double hull construction shall be provided for all cargo holds. A double bottom shall be fitted extending from the collision bulkhead to the aft peak bulk head **.**

**Cargo holds to be designed to have access from upper deck to cargo hold walkways and bilge wells in the aft end. Stringer to be provided as walkway location for each 8’6’’ standard container tiers in hold.**

One (1) pipe duct shall be provided in double bottom from aft end of No.2 cargo hold compartment to fore end of engine room. ***Small hatch covers in place in fore and aft end of pipe duct.***

Pipe duct to be fitted with trolley and sufficient lighting to be also provided.

One (1) set of bow thruster to be installed in bow thruster room..

Mooring facilities shall be arranged as shown on the G.A. plan.

1.2.2 intended cargo

The Vessel shall be designed for carrying container in all cargo holds and on deck.

The types and dimensions of dry cargo containers to be shown as below:

Type of container

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Type | Height  ft-inches | Width  ft-inches | Length  ft-inches |
| ISO-1AA | 8 - 6 | 8 | 40 |
| ISO-1CC | 8 - 6 | 8 | 20 |
| ISO-1AAA | 9 - 6 | 8 | 40 |
| ISO-1EEE | 9 - 6 | 8 | 45 |

Dimension of container

|  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Type | Height | | Width | | Length | | Weight |
| (mm) | Tole-rance  (mm) | (mm) | Tole-rance  (mm) | (mm) | Tole-rance  (mm) | Gross Max.  (MT) |
| ISO-1AA | 2,591 | +0  –5 | 2438 | +0  –5 | 12,192 | +0,-10 | 30.48 |
| ISO-1CC | 2,591 | 6,058 | +0,-6 | 30.48 |
| ISO-1AAA | 2,896 | 12,192 | +0,-10 | 30.48 |
| ISO-1EEE | 2,896 | 13,716 | +0,-10 | 30.48 |

Dangerous goods

Dangerous goods can be carried in closed freight containers in hold and on deck as qualified as follows.

| Loading space  IMO Class | In cargo hold No.1  \*1) | In cargo hold No.2 ~ No.4  \*2,4) | On hatch covers \*3) | Above E/R |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1.1 to 1.6 explosives | X | X | P \*4)7) | X |
| 1.4S | C | C | C | C |
| 2.1 including hydrogen and hydrogen mixtures | X | X | C | X |
| 2.1 excluding hydrogen and hydrogen mixtures | C | X | C | X |
| 2.2 | | C | C | C | X |
| 2.3 flammable | X | X | C | X |
| 2.3 non-flammable | X | X | C | X |
| 3 F.P.<23℃ | C | X | C | X |
| 3 23℃≤F.P.≤60℃ | | C | C | C | X |
| 4.1 | | C | C | C | X |
| 4.2 | | C | C | C | X |
| 4.3 liquids F.P.<23℃ | X | X | C | X |
| 4.3 liquids F.P.≥23℃ | | C | C | C | X |
| 4.3 solids | | C | C | C | X |
| 5.1 | | C | C | C | P\*5) |
| 5.2 | X | X | C | X |
| 6.1 liquids F.P.<23℃ | C | X | C | X |
| 6.1 liquids 23℃≤F.P.≤60℃ | C | C | C | X |
| 6.1 liquids non-flammable | C | C | C | C |
| 6.1 solids | | C | C | C | C |
| 8 liquids F.P.<23℃ | C | X | C | X |
| 8 liquids 23℃≤F.P.≤60℃ | C | C | C | X |
| 8 liquids non-flammable having a subsidiary risk class 6.1 | C | C | C | C |
| 8 solids | | C | C | C | C |
| 9 including goods evolving flammable vapour | X | X | C | X |
| 9 except goods evolving flammable vapour \*6) | C | C | C | C |

Notes:

F.P.: Flash point

C: Intended for carriage

X: Not intended

P \*x): Intended for carriage subject to \*x)

\*1) For cargo hold No.1, explosion-proof type fans to be of IIB-T4 grade or equivalent. If any dangerous cargoes require explosion-proof grade higher than IIB-T4, such cargoes cannot be loaded (i.e. hydrogen, hydrogen mixture, ethyl nitrite, ethyl nitrate, etc.).

\*2) For cargo hold No.2~ No.4, fans to be of non-explosion-proof type.

\*3) Reefer containers on weather deck to be stowed 3m away from the mechanical

ventilation outlet of dangerous cargo hold (No.1) where dangerous cargo is loaded.

\*4) Stow 3m horizontally away from the machinery space boundaries and not be

stowed within a horizontal distance of 6 m from potential sources of ignition in all case.

\*5) Except goods stowage away from sources of heat.

\*6) On examination into nature of dangerous goods and equipment of this vessel, judge

whether is able to stow or not.

\*7) Class 1 (except 1.4S) not to be stowed within a horizontal distance of 6 m from

potential sources of ignition in all case.

1.2.5 DEADWEIGHT, AND CAPACITY

#### 1.2.5.1 Deadweight

The deadweight of the Vessel shall be approx.23940 tons at scantling draught 10.0m, with even keel, with the vessel afloat in sea water with specific gravity of 1.025.

#### 1.2.5.2 Container Capacity

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Capacity of Maximized Container | | | |
|  | 20ft | 40ft | Total  (equivalent to TEU) |
| On deck | 1245 |  | 1245 |
| In hold | 644 | - | 644 |
| Total | 1889 |  | 1889 |
|  | | | |

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Capacity of Self-contained Reefer Container (ISO-1AAA type) | | |
|  | Cooling type | 40ft high cube |
| On deck | Air cooled | 220 |
| In hold | Air cooled | 0 |
| Total |  | 220 |

1. IMO visibility requirement at the scantling draught with even keel is considered in the above mentioned container capacity.
2. Containers shall be stowed in maximum five(5) tiers by ten (10) rows in holds and maximum seven(7) tiers by eleven(11) rows on hatch covers and maximum seven(7)tiers by eleven (11) rows on upper deck.
3. 45ft container (45’ x 8’ x 9’6”) could be stowed on top of 40ft container above hatch

covers where available as shown on the G.A. plan.

1. Maximum clear height of cargo hold shall be based on three (3) tiers of 9’6” high cube container and two (2) tiers of 8’6” container.
2. Reefer slots shall be provided in two (2) tiers on hatch covers and on upper deck as shown on the G.A. plan
3. Number of tiers in the outmost rows of containers on hatch cover / upper deck may be adjusted according to Maker's lashing force calculation result.
4. The final stack weight and weight distribution of the containers on upper deck /hatch covers shall be determined according to lashing force calculation result.
5. Above mentioned number of containers may be decreased/increased in the course of the design development according to final hull lines and G.A. plan.

#### 1.2.5.3 Container Homogeneous Intake

The number of loadable containers of homogeneous 14MT / TEU (ISO 20’ x 8’ x 8’6’’) at scantling draught 10.0m with moderate trim by stern (not more than 1.0% L.O.A.) shall be about 1332TEU with 100% consumables at departure and VCG of 45% container height.

#### 1.2.5.4. Tank Capacity

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Heavy fuel oil /low sulpher heavy fuel oil/Ultra low sulphur fuel oil tanks  (including settling, service tanks) | approx.1,100 m3 |
| Marine Gas Oil tanks (including service tank) | approx.200m3 |
| Fresh Water tanks | approx.200m3 |
| Ballast Water tanks (including anti-heeling tanks) | approx.8300 m3 |

Notes:

1. All the volumes of tanks in above table to be of geometric net volume without actual filling ratio considered.
2. The volume of water ballast tanks specified above means only total geometric volume and some of the specified volume may not be utilized in ballast conditions to achieve proper trim and to avoid any excessive structural stress with the detail design development.

The propeller shall be designed at the power of ME CSR and revolution with about 4%-7% light running margin at design draught 8.50 m with clean hull and propeller in open calm sea.

Propeller strength shall be designed based on SMCR of M/E.

#### 1.2.7.3 Service Speed

The design service speed is about18.5 knots**,** based on:

* On design draught 8.50 m
* Main Engine running at CSR (90% SMCR)
* With 15% sea margin
* Clean hull
* In open, deep sea with Beaufort 0, Douglas sea state 0

Energy saving design:

The rudder bulb to be designed optimized together with propeller. The hull lines, propeller and rudder with rudder bulb to be finally decided by towing tank test.

1.2.8 m/e FUEL CONSUMPTION

The designed M/E Daily fuel oil consumption (D.F.O.C.) is about 35.69t，based on:

The Brake Specified Fuel Consumption (B.S.F.C) of the main engine is about 159.0 grams/kWh (excluding M/E supplier’s tolerance) at CSR（9342kW） based on the use of fuel oil with L.C.V. of 42,700 kJ/kg at ISO 3046-1:2002(E) and ISO 15550:2002(E) ambient condition and fulfilling the IMO NOx emission limitation Tier II (ME back pressure max. 60mbar), which shall be determined by shop test.

Only Brake Specified Fuel Consumption (B.S.F.C) of the main engine based on above-mentioned conditions determined by shop test shall be Contract guaranteed.

In case the shop test conditions are different from the above, the results shall be corrected in accordance with the manufacture’s standards.

1.2.9 CRUISING rANGE

About 11,000n.miles, assuming:

- ISO ambient conditions

- Main Engine running at CSR (90% SMCR)

- Service speed of 18.5 knots on design draught

- Fuel oil consumption for main engine and one (1) set of generator engine power supply at basic hotel load (including tolerance 5% of SFOC)

- Fuel oil with specific gravity of 1.01 tons/ m3 for HFO, 0.99 tons/m3 for LSHFO/ULSFO, 40,600kJ/kg in L.C.V. and 0.89 tons/ m3 for MGO, 42,707kJ/kg in L.C.V.

- 98% full of fuel oil tanks

- Including all HFO,LSHFO/ULSFO /MGO storage, settling and service tanks

1.2.10 FREEBOARD

The Vessel shall be designed according to the requirement of the International Convention on Load Lines (ICLL), 1966 revised by protocol 1988 and all latest amendments for type "B" ship.

## 1.3 RULES AND REGULATIONS

1.3.1 CLASSIFICATION

The Vessel including its hull, machinery, equipment and outfitting shall be built under the supervision of Classification Society (hereinafter called the "Class") and shall be distinguished in the record by the notation of:

***NK NS\* (CNC, EQ C DG, PSPC-WBT, NC) (IWS) (PSCM) (EA) (CSSA-R) (IHM) (Sox(EGCS)) MNS\*(M0)***

***Installation Character(s): BWM, MPP, LSA, RCF, M0, AFS***

***Loading computer will be approved by class.***

However, the Class rule shall be applied with the latest version at the date of the Contract signing.

1.3.2 FLAG

The Vessel shall be registered under the flag of ***Marshall*** .

1.3.3 RULES AND REGULATIONS

## 1.4 PROPERTIES OF THE VESSEL

1.4.1 MODEL TEST

The model tests consist of the following items which shall be carried out at SSSRI (Shanghai Ship& Shipping Research Institute) and / or CSSRC (China Ship Scientific Research Center).

1. Resistance test, at the sea trial ballast draught / EEDI draught / design draught / scantling draught (4draughts), six (6) speeds.
2. Self-propulsion test with design propeller at sea trial ballast draught / EEDI draught / design draught / scantling draught (4draughts), six (6) speeds.
3. Open water test of design propeller
4. Stream line paint test for bilge keel at service speed on design draught
5. 3-D Wake field measurement at service speed on design draught
6. Designed propeller cavitation test with pressure fluctuation measurement at service speed on design draught and trial ballast draught. ***The rudder cavitation can be observed together, and the cavitation report will be provided including the rudder cavitation description.***

Model test reports shall be submitted to the Buyer for reference only.

EEDI verification shall be carried out according to IMO Resolution MEPC.254(67) and ISO 15016:2015(E).

The Builder will inform the Buyer to attend model test. The fee that Buyer attend model test are on Buyer’s account.

1.4.2 deadweight and lightweight

The deadweight shall be the difference between the lightweight and fully loaded displacement in sea water of specific gravity of 1.025.

“Fully loaded displacement” is the total displacement in metric tons at the draught specified in “1.2.3 Principal Dimensions” in sea water of specific gravity of 1.025 including shell and all appendages, under the condition of even keel, no heel, no deflection of the Vessel.

The following items shall belong to the lightweight:

* Hull, outfitting, machinery and electric weights, including the weight of fittings and equipment as stated in the Specification;
* Spare parts and inventories according to the requirement of Classification Society and other contractual Regulatory Bodies;
* Oil and water inside the machinery, heat exchangers, supplying/circulating piping and valves in engine room directly related to main engine based on the minimum quantity necessary for main engine starting.
* Fixed fire-fighting mediums (CO2, dry chemical powder, foam concentrate, fresh water, etc.) as per IMO MSC.1/Circ.1539

All weight including the following other than those mentioned above shall belong to the deadweight:

* Cargo and/or ballast water (including water in ballast pipe);
* All fuel oil(HFO/LSHFO/ULSFO/MGO), lubrication oil and fresh water including stern tube cooling water;
* Spare parts and inventories in excess of the requirement of the Classification Society and other contractual Regulatory Bodies;
* Equipment, spare parts and tools supplied by the Buyer in excess of the Rules and Regulations;
* Tools and test equipment;
* Crew, luggage and effects on board;
* Provisions;
* Stores of all kinds;
* All loose fittings for containers lashing and securing;
* Cargo lifting beams and grommets;
* All other outfitting items supplied by the Buyer, if any.

1.4.3 TRIM AND STABILITY

The Builder shall carry out trim and stability calculation based on the following criteria and loading conditions.

Criteria (Only for Seagoing conditions):

* 2008 IS Code Part A Chapter 2.2&2.3
* IMO SOLAS II-1, Part B-1 Subdivision and Damage Stability of Cargo Ships
* Trim by stern limited to 1.0%LOA(except ballast conditions)

Loading Conditions:

1. Lightship condition.
2. Docking condition with zero cargo and arrival bunker.
3. Ballast condition with zero cargo, at departure and arrival.
4. Ballast condition with cargo for Panama Canal transit, at departure and arrival.
5. Homogeneous10, 12, 14, 16, 18 MT/TEU container (8’6’’ height) loading condition, at design draught, at departure and arrival.
6. Homogeneous10, 12, 14, 16, 18MT/ TEU container (8’6’’ height) loading condition, at scantling draught, at departure and arrival.

Note:

1) The loadable number of containers shall be limited only by visibility requirements. The restrictions by capability of container lashing and securing system to be not taken into account.

2) Transverse metacentric height after free surface correction (G0M) shall not be less than the minimum GM value required by damage stability.

3) For each calculation, bunker and other consumable supplies shall be as follow

At departure: 100% consumables supplies

At arrival: Approx. 10% supplies forHFO/LSFO/ULSFO/MGO/FW and approx. 70%~85% supplies for LO of the total amount at departure

4) The vertical center of gravity (VCG) for stability calculations shall be assumed 45% of the container height.

5) Following values shall be used for the trim and stability calculation:

Kind of liquid Specific gravity Full filling ratio (%)

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Ballast water: | 1.025 | 100 |
| Fresh water: | 1.000 | 100 |
| Heavy fuel oil: | 1.01 | 98 |
| Low Sulphur Heavy fuel oil/  Ultra Low Sulphur fuel oil | 0. 990 | 98 |
| Marine Gas oil: | 0.890 | 98 |
| Lube. Oil: | 0.900 | 98 |

Ballast water may be loaded fully and/or partially to obtain suitable trim and stability within the permissible shear force and bending moments assigned by the Classification Society.

***The load conditions in the Trim and Stability Booklet shall show the values for each***

***read-out frame, given by the SF&BM&TM limit approval letter. Shear force, bending moment and cargo torsional moment to be used with the same unit as used at the Class approval letter (kN for force and kN.m for moment to be used).***

The Builder shall furnish the final Trim and Stability Booklet based on the lightship property obtained from inclining test or lightweight test.

If the final trim and stability booklet is under the approval stage by the Class or Authority at the delivery time of the Vessel, the preliminary one shall be onboard for provisional use.

1.4.4 VIBRATION AND NOISE LEVEL

#### 1.4.4.1 Vibration Level

The International standard ISO6954-2000(E) “Mechanical vibration-Guidelines for the measurement, reporting and evaluation of vibration with regard to habitability on passenger and merchant ships” shall be used as criteria for the vibrating evaluation in the accommodation and working area (except bridge wings).

The design target for vibration level shall be below the upper limit of the "stippled zone" on the figure of the mentioned ISO standard as far as possible. The vibration levels in living quarters shall be below 6.0 mm/sec for area classification B (crew accommodation areas) and below 8.0 mm/sec for area classification C (working areas) as defined in ISO 6954-2000(E).

The vibration measurement shall be carried out during the sea trial in condition of smooth water with main engine running at the operating rpm specified in CSR condition (1.2.7) of main engine as per the Builder’s practice according to ISO 6954-2000(E).

The vibrations deriving from abnormal sailing conditions such as bad weather, maneuvering, running astern, etc. shall not be taken into account.

If vibration level exceeds the limit as defined by ISO 6954-2000(E), the Builder shall make necessary improvement to a practical extent mutually agreed between the Buyer and the Builder, but without second sea trial unless Flag requires.

#### 1.4.4.2 Noise Level

Sound insulation and isolation treatment shall be provided as necessary to keep noise levels within the following values at normal sea going condition within the limit as defined by IMO Resolution MSC.337(91)–“Adoption of the code on noise levels on board ships” (only mandatory part) (Except bridge wing).

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Designation of rooms and spaces | dB(A) |
| Machinery space | 110 |
| Engine control room | 75 |
| Work shop out of machinery space | 85 |
| Wheelhouse including chart space | 65 |
| Private cabin | 55 |
| Mess room, recreation room and office | 60 |
| Hospital | 55 |
| Galley and pantry (without food processing equipment operating) | 75 |
| Look-out posts including bridge wings and windows | 70 |

The noise level measurement shall be carried out according to IMO Resolution MSC.337(91). During sea trial, the Vessel shall be running ahead steadily at the operating rpm specified at CSR of main engine, and not less than 80% of the specified maximum continuous rating (SMCR), under the following conditions, and the bedding and linen as well as personal goods shall not be removed during these measurements:

* Auxiliary engine(s) shall be operated in normal sea going condition without reefer containers.
* Machinery unnecessary for normal navigation shall be stopped.
* Mechanical ventilation and air-conditioning equipment shall be in normal operation.
* All doors and windows of the rooms shall be closed.
* No intermittent sound and noise shall be included (i.e. from air horn, sanitary flushing, laundry machine, emergency generator, telephone, speaker, foot-step noise in stair and corridor space, etc.)
* The measurement shall be taken at a height of 1.2 m to 1.6 m above deck, platform or walkway according to IMO Regulation.

If the measured noise level exceeds the specified value as required by Resolution MSC.337(91) by more than 3 dB(A), the Builder shall make necessary improvement to a practical extent mutually agreed between the Buyer and the Builder, but without second sea trial.

## 1.5 INSPECTION, TESTING AND TRIAL

1.5.1 GENERAL

The inspection, testing and trial during construction of the Vessel shall be carried out by the Builder and/or the Maker at Maker’s shop or onboard as per the Builder’s and/or the Maker’s practice in compliance with the Rules requirements of the Classification Society under the presence of the Buyer's supervisor(s) and/or the Surveyor of the Classification Society.

The list of items for inspection and testing shall be submitted to the Buyer for approval in advance.

In section schedule shall be submitted to the Buyer's supervisor(s) one (1) working day in advance, if inspection takes place inside shipyard or near shipyard. And seven (7) working days in advance for the inspection outside shipyard in China, and fourteen (14) calendar days in advance for the inspection out of China. Builder will provide the weekly schedule in advance.

Failure of the Buyer's supervisor(s) present, without justifiable reason after due notice as above, shall be deemed as the waiver of the right, and in such case the Buyer shall be obliged to accept the result so such test on the basis of the Builder's and the Classification Society’s reports on the said results.

Any different opinion of inspection or test between the Buyer’s supervisor and the Builder’s supervisor shall refer to the opinion of Classification Society Surveyor as the settlement.

As to the details of testing of hull, machinery and electrical equipment and installations, refer to relevant Parts.

1.5.2 INSPECTION AND TEST OF CONSTRUCTION

Tests and inspection for hull structure shall be conducted in accordance with the Rules requirement of the Classification Society, IACS Rec.47 and the agreed CSQS and/or the Builder’s standard at time of Contract. ***List of item for inspection to be submitted to owner.***

**Records with all measurements during inspections, tests and trials (for all hull /machinery / outfitting /electrical fields) to be prepared by the builder and submitted to the Buyer as a single finished quality booklet.**

**The Builder/ Subcontractor is to ensure safe access for all inspections.**

The block inspection to be carried out after completion of hull block steel works. Even if fittings are fitted wholly or partially to the hull blocks, the inspection for the hull blocks shall be carried out without dismantling such fittings unless the block inspection is obstructed by such fittings.

Castings of stern frame and rudder to be tested by magnaflux or equivalent according to rule's requirement.

***Up to total 20 X-rays/UT in addition to class requirements will be taken upon request of Buyer's supervisors and will be marked by Buyer's supervisors on the NDT drawing. if any defect area(such as working hole/or repair area), to be done NDT inspection according to class requirement.***

**List of tanks that will not be hydrostatically tested shall be provided to buyer during plan approval.**

**Piping tests to be carried out in two steps: Checking of system’s construction and flushing or blowing. Tightness test as per Class and Maker’s requirements and recommendations.**

1.5.3 SHOP TESTS

Shop tests for main engine, auxiliary machineries, boiler, deck machineries, provision crane, steering gear, boat davit, control console, etc. to be performed in accordance with the Rule’s requirement and/or the Maker’s standard. The items of shop test to be according to Class’s requirement and Maker's standard. ***Other machineries also same the M/E+G/E must inform to owner shop test day and test record.***

The shop tests of main engine, main generator sets and main switchboard to be attended by the Buyer. The Buyer shall be informed of the shop test schedule at least fourteen (14) calendar days in advance out of China and seven (7) calendar days in advance in China in general of the expected date of the shop tests. The Buyer’s attendance shall be confirmed to the Builder at least seven (7) calendar days in advance out of China and two(2) working days in advance in China of the expected date of the shop test. The list of the Buyer plans to join shop test will be mutually agreed by both sides and submitted later. ***Other machineries test must inform to owner shop test day and test record.***

The detailed descriptions of shop tests shall be also referred to respective Specifications.

The guarantee fuel consumption of the main engine to be certified at the Maker’s shop test.

1.5.4 MOORING TEST and lifting test of container

Items for mooring test to be submitted to the Buyer four (4) weeks ahead of the test. Procedure for mooring test of the Vessel shall be submitted to the Buyer for review.

The container stowage test for cell-guide in cargo holds and container sockets on deck to be carried out for each 20ftand 40ft socket.

**Calibrated container to be used and test carried out in the presence of buyer representative. In case the container test for hatch cover is done at factory, the test to be repeated at random on board for not less than 30% of sockets. *Others socket will be check by scanner or total station equipment.***

1.5.5 INCLINING TEST AND lightWEIGHT MEASUREMENT

When the Vessel is substantially completed except minor items of work, an inclining test and deadweight measurement shall be carried out in order to determine the lightship weight and center of gravity of the Vessel as per the Builder’s practice. **Inclining Test Procedure to be prepared by the Shipyard according to Class requirements and in line with IACS REC.031.**

#### 1.5.5.1 Inclining Test

The inclining test shall be carried out in the presence of the Buyer's Supervisor(s) and the Classification Society’s Surveyor in accordance with the procedure of inclining test and deadweight measurement.

The inclining test shall be conducted by shifting solid portable weights on upper deck or hatch cover and by measuring the Vessel's heeling angle using U-tubes or pendulums which placed forward and aft of the cargo hold region.

The results shall be submitted to the Classification Society for approval. The report shall be furnished to the Buyer.

For subsequent vessel(s) of this series, the inclining test except lightweight survey shall not be carried out and the results of the first Vessel shall be referred to subject to approval by the Classification Society.

#### 1.5.5.2 Lightweight Survey

For subsequent vessel(s) of this series, the inclining test except lightweight survey shall not be carried out and the results of the first Vessel shall be referred to subject to approval by the Classification Society if the deviation of lightweight of sister vessel(s) with first Vessel is not more than 1%.

Lightweight survey shall be carried out by visual reading the draught of the Vessel, by measuring specific gravity of water and by subtracting the weight temporarily loaded items on board and adding the weight of unfurnished items at the time of lightweight survey in the presence of the Buyer’s Supervisor(s) and the Classification Society’s Surveyor.

Draught of the Vessel shall be read at the port and starboard side in way of fore, midship and aft draught marks.

The displacement of the Vessel shall be determined from the hydrostatic tables based on the measured draughts with due corrections for trim, heel, deflection of the Vessel and specific gravity of water at the measurement according to the Builder’s practice.

1.5.6 QUAY TRIAL and sea trial

#### 1.5.6.1 Quay Trial

Quay trial for the main engine shall be carried out to check the starting and running of main engine with associated auxiliary machinery prior to the sea trials while the Vessel is moored at the Builder's quay according to Builder’s practice.

* Confirmation of starting position
* Turning gear interlock test
* Confirmation of control test
* Safety device test (automatic trip by simulation)
* Minimum revolution test
* Inspection of crankcase
* Test of starting air capacity

Following test shall be carried out during Quay trial or Official Sea trial.

* Anchoring test
* Lifeboat and davit operation test, launching test
* Refrigerating system test
* Air conditioning system test
* Ballast and bilge system test
* Ballast water treatment plant test
* Emergency fire pump test
* Black-out test

#### 1.5.6.2 Sea Trial

When the vessel is substantially completed and ready for sea trial (excluding works which can be made after sea trial), sea trial to be performed by the Builderand mutually agreed program in the presence of the Owner’s representative and the Class surveyor.

Reports of official sea trial shall be submitted to the Buyer.

After sea trial, working parts of main engine and auxiliary machinery to be opened for the Buyer's inspection on Buyer’s request which cylinder to be opened in accordance with the standard of the Builder, approved by Buyer and refitted to working condition. A confirmation dock run after overhaul for 1/2 hours at low load to be carried out before delivery.

Marine diesel oil (MDO) and heavy fuel oil (HFO) of RMK380 available viscosity in

Chinese domestic commercial market shall be used for the sea trial at the Builder’s

decision. MDO ***(viscosity is 3~6 cSt/40oC (Sulfur content <0.1% m/m)*** will be used instead of MGO for MGO system function test.

The test condition of Scrubber in sea trial should be done as below:

1) The alkalinity of the sea water: according to the actual sea trail area.

2) The sulphur value of the fuel oil: according to the actual filling fuel oil (2.5~3.5%.).

3) The engine loading to be as following

For ME: 100%SMCR (to be carried out as per engine output power or engine revolution which reach first).

For AE: according to the actual consumption in the sea trial condition.

Duration: One(1) hour

Sea trial shall be carried out at the ballast condition corresponding to model test.

The measured trial speed shall be corrected to no wind and no wave, open, deep and current less sea conditions as per ISO 15016:2015(E) - "Guidelines for the assessment of speed and power performance by analysis of speed trial data".

The service speed at design draught under the conditions defined in Section 2-7.3 shall be obtained by means of extrapolation based on the above corrected speed and model test results.

During the sea trial following test and trial, as well as other items required by the Classification Society and/or the Regulation Bodies concerned shall be conducted.

| Item | M/E Load | 1st Vessel | Subsequent Vessel (s) | Remark |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Test condition | - | Ballast draught | Ballast draught | - |
| Progressive speed |  |  |  |  |
| 65% | O | O | \*1 |
| 75% | O | O | \*1 |
| CSR | O | O | \*1\*8 |
| SMCR | O | O | \*1\*8 |
| Endurance test  (Duration: two (2) hours at CSR and four (4) hours at SMCR plus 30 minutes at 103.2% normal propeller speed where engine adjustment permits.) | CSR | O | O | \*2 |
| Maneuvering test | | | |  |
| - Turning circle test | \*3 | O | X | \*5 |
| - Zig-Zag test | \*3 | O | X | 10°/10° |
| - Crash stop astern test | \*3 cond. To full astern | O | O | \*4 |
| - Inertia test | CSR | O | X | \*7, \*9 |
| - Williamson turning test | CSR | O | X | \*7 |
| Measurement of noise level (during endurance test) | CSR | O | O | \*7 |
| Measurement of hull local vibration | CSR | O | X | \*7 |
| Steering gear test | SMCR | O | O | \*7 |
| Anchoring equipment test | - | O | O |  |
| Bow thruster test | - | O | O |  |
| Tests and calibration or adjustment of navigation equipment and instruments such as magnetic compass, auto pilot, echo sounder, speed log and radar, etc. | - | O | O |  |

| Main engine overhaul inspection after sea trial \*9 | - | O | O |  |
| Dead ship recovery test |  | O | O |  |
| Change over for M/E,G/Es and boiler from HFO-MDO (Statement to be certified by Classification Society) |  | O | O |  |

Notes:

“O” means “do”; “X” means “not do”

\*1: Trial running on each load of main engine shall be of at least one (1) double run consisting of one (1) run in a direction on the course and one (1) run in the opposite direction.

Speed tests for final verification of attained EEDI to be during progressive speed tests.

The Vessel's speed shall be measured by means of Differential Global Positioning System (DGPS).

Weather condition of wind velocity and significant wave height shall be in accordance with requirement of ISO 15016:2015(E). The speed trial shall be carried out under the weather condition of maximum Beaufort Scale 5.

The measuring of main engine power of the Vessel shall be done by the Builder’s torsion meter.

\*2: Fuel consumption of main engine shall be measured for ten (10) minutes at CSR during the endurance test for reference. The Brake Specified Fuel Consumption (B.S.F.C) of the main engine at shop test to be guaranteed.Endurance trial to be carried to be carried out as per engine output power instead of engine revolution except that Endurance trial at 90%SMCR and 100% SMCR to be carried out as per engine output power or engine revolution which reach first.

\*3: The test speed for Maneuvering test is at the operating rpm specified at CSR of main engine and complying with the IMO MSC.137(76).

\*4: To stop the Vessel (Until ahead speed becomes zero).

\*5: To port and starboard with 35 deg. of rudder angle.

\*6: Main engine RPM range for torsional vibration test to be decided according to manufacturer’s recommendation.

\*7: Operating RPM at the specified power

\*8: As per engine output power or engine revolution at the specified power which reach first.

\*9: To stop the Vessel (Until ahead speed to become approx. 6 knots)

## 1.6 DOCUMENTATION

1.6.1 PLANS FOR APPROVAL

The plans for Buyer's approval shall be in accordance with the “List of drawing for Buyer's approval” ***with approximate dates*** as agreed between Builder and Buyer and submitted to the Buyer for approval after the Building Contract of the Vessel.

Electronic copy (PDF format) of the plans for approval shall be submitted to the Buyer and the plans with the Buyer's approved signature shall be returned to the Builder. And these returned plans should be clearly marked with“approved” or “approved with comments” or “not approved”.

The Builder’s standard Plans and subcontractor’s or Maker’s Plans may be used as working plans or plans for approval.

The plans submitted for approval shall be deemed to have been approved without any comment when the Buyer does not dispatch the approved plan within fourteen(14) calendar days after receipt the electronic copy plans.

After the mutual agreement of each drawing's/manual's comments, included in the relevant PCF form, a revised drawing called "Final Agreed Drawing", should be submitted to Owners which will include all the modifications agreed during the plan approval stage and all class comments, if any. This "Final Agreed Drawing", shall be the

one to be used during the vessel's construction stage.

During the phase of class plan approval, Builder will provide the Class approval drawing with class’ comments to the Buyer.

Final Approved drawings as clean version shall be submitted in one set of hard copy and

PDF electronic format to the Site office well in advance before onsite inspections. These

drawings to be in English.

For sister vessels, if any, the plans and documents of first vessel shall be used, so no duplication of drawing approval shall be necessary in general.

1.6.2 FINISHED DRAWINGS

Upon delivery of the Vessel, ***four (4)*** copies in black and white of finished plans shall be furnished to the Buyer in accordance with “List of finished plans”, one (1) copy to the Buyer’s office and two (2) copies to the Vessel.

The scope and form of the finished plans shall be in accordance with the Builder’s standard and the list of finished plans shall be submitted to the Buyer for approval in due course.

One (1) set of the final plans except Maker’s plans shall be furnished to the Buyer in electronic PDF format (CD-ROM or equivalent) in accordance with “List of finished plans” for the first vessel.

Instruction books shall be furnished for equipment and machinery, as supplied by manufacturer. Electronic manual of M/E and A/E to be provided by Maker.

The following plans, one (1) copy for each, mounted in aluminum alloy frame with glass shall be arranged at suitable places on board as directed by Buyer's supervisor. ***Except GA Plan and Fire Control and Safety Plan submit three(3) copy for Bridge, A-deck and ECR.***

1. General Arrangement Plan
2. Tank Capacity Plan with Deadweight Scale
3. Container Stowage Plan
4. Fire Control and Safety Plan in color coding (Class approved)
5. Damage Control Plan (1:200)
6. Ballast and Bilge Pumping Plan
7. Fuel Oil Bunker Procedure
8. Fuel Oil Transfer System Plan
9. Muster List (Buyer supply)
10. Maneuvering Characteristics Diagram with time and distance (comply with IMO Res.A601)

1.6.3 EXHIBITION MODEL

One (1) exhibition model for series vessel in the scale of 1: 200 shall be supplied to the Buyer’s site office.

## 1.7 DRY DOCKING

In the event that the period between the launching and the delivery date of the Vessel is more than six (6) months, an underwater survey shall be carried out. The diving company should be certified by Class. If the condition of the underwater survey is acceptable by painting maker, and maker provide 60 months guarantee, then no dry docking will be carried out. Otherwise, docking and hull cleaning at Builder's cost and time is to be carried out. **The Paint maker must give a guarantee that vessel can remain 6 months in water prior delivery and 60 month Guarantee is applicable from date of delivery.**

.

If the period from launching to delivery exceed more than 8 months, the vessel will be dry docking.

## 1.8 LOAD instrument

One (1) set of loading computer with software approved by the class with certificate to be supplied by buyer.

UPS to be supplied for loading computer. Loading computer with printer to be provided in ship’s office.

The calculation functions and display of the loading computer shall consist of:

1. Displacement
2. Trim/draught (fore and aft)
3. Draft correction (fore and aft) due to difference of sea water density
4. Shear force and bending moment at the prescribed frame points
5. Maximum value of shear force and bending moment at the frame point
6. Intact stability calculation and check of damage stability(by minimum GM/ maximum KG)
7. Torsional strength
8. Summary of loading condition
9. Trim adjustment by ballast tank (program)
10. Navigation bridge visibility

Lashing (if required):

1. Container loading calculation by weight
2. Lashing strength and racking force calculation
3. Container control program

Data of tank level to be automatically transmitted from the ballast and bunkering control system.
