# CHAPTER 4 OUTFITTING

## 4.1 anchoring AND MOORING EQUIPMENT

### 4.1.1 Deck Machinery in General

The arrangement of windlass and mooring winch shall be in accordance with the requirement of the Classification Society ***and Panama Canal regulations of 2020***. Final arrangement of winches and mooring fittings shall subject to detailed Mooring Fitting Arrangement Plan during detail design stage.

Electric hydraulic type deck machinery with auto-tension device for mooring drum shall be provided as shown on the G.A. plan.

Electric heater to be provided for electrical motor of deck machinery.

Gear for cable lifter part shall be of open type with steel cover for dust protection and gear for mooring winches shall be of enclosed type.

The mooring drum shall be of split type and large enough to wind the required mooring rope of not less than ***220*** m long and 64mm diameter(size subject to maker’s recommendation) on storage of the drum.

Warping head shall be of cast iron smooth barrel tube type and shall be directly connected to driving shaft without clutching device.

**Protection *plate or pipe* to be provided on top of the hydraulic motor especially if the motor is axial piston type.**

Each cable lifter and mooring drum shall be fitted with two (2) halves type hand operated friction band brake and clutch operated locally. Brake drum surface for cable lifter and mooring drum shall be of mild steel. **Break lining wear indication method to be provided as per maker’s standard.**

**Grease nipple to be provided for greasing the pin of brake bands and all pins. Grease**

**nipples to be of the same type as far as possible.**

Seat of cable lifters shall be of open type with height as low as possible.

Steel chock for cable lifters and resin chock for mooring winches shall be used for the liner of foundation.

The windlass/mooring winch shall be operated by local control. The control handle combined with a control stand shall be provided near the driving motor of each windlass and mooring winch at each machine side for local control. The clutch of mooring winch shall be provided with manual control device at machine side for local control.

Shipside remote control stand for the mooring winch to be provided with following function:

For mooring winch: remote control stand shall be combined with auto-tension control, speed, emergency stop, direction change

Material, construction, spare parts, etc. shall be in accordance with the manufacturer's standards and shall comply with requirements of Classification Society.

The stainless steel name plate shall be provided for each combined windlass/mooring winch and mooring winch.

***Snap back zones to be indicated on the mooring arrangements and paint marked on deck.***

***It is safe practice to provide rope guard around the mooring winch operation platform.***

***All platforms frame for windlass and winches to be galvanized open grating***

### 4.1.2 WINDLASS AND MOORING WINCH

#### 4.1.2.1 Combined Windlass/Mooring Winch

Two (2) sets of combined windlass/mooring winch of independent type shall be located at forecastle deck.

Each combined windlass/mooring winch shall be composed of, one (1) declutchable cable lifter, two(2) declutchable mooring drum and one (1) warping head.

Gypsy wheel and mooring drum shall not be operated simultaneously.

The mooring drum shall be designed to take one whole rope on six (6) or seven (7) layers, declutched to the shaft and operated through clutch.

Brake holding force of windlass shall be sufficient in accordance with the requirements of Classification Society.

***It has to be ensured that all flanges of the hydraulic pipes at the pumping station and on deck near the windlass and mooring winches fall with in the oil coaming.***

Particulars of each combined windlass/mooring winch shall be as follows.

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Item | Gypsy | Mooring drum | Warping head |
| Quantity | 1 | 2 | 1 |
| Capacity | A rated line pull in compliance with the requirement of the Classification Society at average hoisting speed of about 9m/min | per drum abt.15tx15m/min  (on the first layer) | abt.15t |
| Standard for chain, rope and capacity | Φ70, Grade 3 chain of welding. Joining shackles shall be of Kenter type | Φ64x ***220m*** rope (size subject to maker’s recommendation)  With min. strength abt.638KN | six(6) turns |

#### 4.1.2.2 Mooring Winch

Two (2) sets of mooring winch shall be provided. ***Mooring winches to be split type drums.***

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Location | Quantity | Combination | |
| Mooring drum | Warping head |
| deck aft. | 2 | 2 | 1 |

Particulars:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Item | drum | Warping head |
| Rated Capacity | Abt. 15 t x 15 m/min | abt.15 t |
| Rope capacity and standard | Φ64 x ***220m***(size subject to maker’s recommendation) | 6 turns |

The rated capacity of each mooring winch shall be obtained on the first layer of the drum at operation of single drum.

Slack rope speed shall comply with manufacturer's standards and Rule/Regulations of Classification Society.

### 4.1.3 ANCHOR and CHAIN CABLE

The equipment in accordance with Rules requirements shall be provided.

#### 4.1.3.1 Anchor and Chain Cable

Two (2) bower anchors of stockless, SPEK type shall be provided for each vessel. Each weight is 6225 kg.

Anchor chain cable shall be of flush butt welded stud link, grade 3 type and provided in accordance with the requirement of the Classification Society.

The diameter of the anchor chain cable shall be 70mm and total length shall be 632.5m as per Rule requirement. Anchor chain cable shall be jointed with Kenter type shackle at every 27.5 m length. A swivel piece shall be fitted at each extreme outboard end of the anchor chain cable.

Anchor chain cable shall be marked with red paint at every Kenter shackle and white paint at same number of common links as shot numbers and stainless steel (SUS304) band tape at each last common link.

End link of chain cable shall be fastened to cable clench located outside each chain locker. These shall be released manually from bosun store in an emergency.

Accessories for anchor chain shall be supplied according to Maker’s standard in compliance with Rules ***and as below***

***6 - Chain hook***

***2 – Pin punch***

***1 – Shackle punch***

***2 – Spare kenter shackle***

***1 – Spare end shackle***

***1 – Spare taper pin for anchor shackle***

***3 – Spare taper pin for kenter shackle***

***1 – Pin hammer***

***1 – Shackle hammer***

***1 – Disengaging tool for kenter shackle***

#### 4.1.3.2 Chain Stopper

One (1) set of roller type chain stopper shall be arranged between each hawse pipe and windlass.

The chain stopper shall be of welded steel frame construction with a cast steel roller and a bar type stopper.

Necessary turnbuckle and steel wire rope shall be provided for fastening the anchor chain.

### 4.1.4 HAWSE PIPE AND CHAIN PIPE

#### 4.1.4.1 Hawse Pipe

Location: one(1) at each side of forecastle deck forward.

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Material: | Pipe | Welded steel plate |
|  | Bell mouth | Welded steel plate and cast steel |

Deck flange shall be fitted at the deck openings of the hawse pipes to allow satisfactory housing of the chain cable and easy leading to the gypsy wheel. Attention shall be paid to the anchoring arrangement to obtain good clutch of the chain cables round the cable holders. Fixed guard rails shall be fitted around the deck flanges.

The bell mouth shall extent to outside to ensure the clearance of min. 300 mm between anchor and side shell under ship upright condition on even keel. ***Anchor when stowed in the bell mouth should have 3 point contact.***

Galvanized steel cover plate shall be provided for hawse pipe opening on forecastle deck, and fixed with stainless steel stud-bolt and pin. Three (3) nozzles shall be provided in hawse pipes for cable chain.

Watching platform and protection handrail shall be arranged on the forecastle bulwark in suitable place ***for anchor inspection***.

#### 4.1.4.2 Chain Pipe

Location: one(1) under each gypsy wheel

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Material: | Pipe | Welded steel plate |
|  | Cover | Galvanized steel plate |

Chafing ring of fabricated steel bar on deck and bell-mouth at lower edge shall be fitted for protection and smooth running of cables.

### 4.1.5 mooring fitting AND MOORING ROPE

#### 4.1.5.1 Mooring Rope

Mooring ropes shall be equipped in accordance with the Rules requirements as follows:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Item | No. | Standard |
| Mooring rope | 11 | 64mm dia. x***220m*** floating type (Polypropylene or equivalent material) (size subject to maker’s recommendation)with strength of as per Rules but min. 500kN |
| Towing rope(Buyer’s supply) | 1 | Steel wire, 260m with strength of min.1,471kN |

#### 4.1.5.2 Mooring Fitting

The mooring fittings shall be arranged as symmetric as possible as shown on the G.A. plan.

***Mooring fittings, such as bollard, fairleader, close chock, stand fairleader etc, to be arranged as shown on the G.A plan. ISO or GB standard type mooring fitting will be choosen by design stage.***

Size, number and type of mooring fitting shall be finally determined according to the “Mooring fitting arrangement plan” during detail design stage based on the requirements of Rules.

Construction, material, dimensions etc. of the mooring fittings not specified in the Specification shall be in accordance with the Builder’s standard.

***2-roller or 3-roller type fairleader to be provided. All roller type chocks to be provided with upper roller and/or retaining pipe, in order to avoid rope jumping.***

***All deck rollers to be removed / under surface cleaned and final coat applied prior delivery to avoid rust streaks running from dust trapped underneath during grinding in vicinity as far as possible.***

All moving parts of the fittings shall have bronze bushes and fitted grease nipple. ***The***

***grease gun to be provided and the grease nipples to be of same size/type as far as possible.***

Non-slip paint shall be provided around bollard and rope handling space for anti-slip.

All surfaces of the fittings in contact with the mooring rope shall be ground smoothly so that the mooring rope can be protected from wearing.

Seat of mooring fitting shall be of steel plate and strengthened under deck as per Rules.

Round bar or half round bar shall be fitted on the top of shell plate in way of mooring fitting to protect rope.

The safety working loads to be welded on the equipment.

## 4.2 STEERING SYSTEM

### 4.2.1 STEERING GEAR

One (1) set of electro-hydraulic ram type with 4 cylinders and 2 rams steering gear shall be installed in the steering gear room.

The steering gear shall be capable of turning the rudder from 35 deg. on one side to 30 deg. on the other side within 28 seconds with operation of one of the two (2) pumps (one (1) pump stand by), under the condition that the Vessel runs ahead at the summer load draught with maximum ahead service speed.

The operating angle of the steering gear shall be able to reach maximum 35 degree both sides, and the rudder stoppers shall be fitted on the steering gear to prevent the rudder from being hard over at about 37 degree both sides.

The steering gear shall consist of two (2) electro-hydraulic pump units, each with 100% capacity, and integrated hydraulic piping instruments. If one power unit fails, the remaining unit to be able to operate by change of the gear. One (1) of two power units can be operated at the capacity in accordance with relevant rule by emergency electric power supplied from emergency generator in case of the main electric power failure.

Each pump unit shall be equipped with a hydraulic oil pump, an IP44 type squirrel cage electric motor and a hydraulic oil tank with a low level alarm switch.

***Each one pump unit in sea trial for testing to be output 100%.***

The power unit shall be started/stopped from the wheelhouse and the steering gear room.

In case of main power failure, the power shall be automatically supplied from emergency generator to steering gear within 45 seconds in compliance with the Rules and Regulations.

A notice plate for emergency operation shall be provided in steering gear room and wheelhouse.

The steering gear shall be controlled by the steering control system (auto pilot) in the wheelhouse. In addition, the steering gear also shall be provided with a manual control device in the steering gear room for emergency operation in case of failure of control system.

The remote control and rudder angle indicator of the steering gear shall be provided in the wheelhouse and bridge wings, and the remote rudder angle indicator shall be provided in the engine control room.

The piping between the pumps and cylinders shall be seamless steel.

The hydraulic system of the steering gear shall be flushed at the manufacturer’s shop according to their standard, and then shall be properly protected during transportation and installation.

A fixed hydraulic oil storage tank with manual pump ready shall be provided in the steering gear room for recharge of the system as required by the Rule.

The mechanical type rudder angle indicator shall be fitted on the steering gear body. The rudder angle indicator shall be independent of the steering gear control system, and be readily visible from all control positions.

A gyro repeater shall be installed in the steering gear room readable from the manual control stand.

The construction, materials, accessories, etc., shall be in compliance with the requirements of the Classification Society and the manufacturer’s standards unless otherwise specified.

Lifting eyes shall be fitted underneath of upper deck for maintenance of the steering gear.

Working platform with handrail shall be provided around the steering gear for easy accessibility.

Non-slip paint (width : 1 m) shall be provided from the entrance of the steering gear room to the steering gear in compliance with the Rules and Regulations.

Steel coaming of about 100 mm high shall be provided around the steering gear.

Steel chock or resin chock shall be used for liner of steering gear foundation according to Maker’s recommendation.

### 4.2.2 RUDDER AND RUDDER STOCK AND OTHERS

Rudder to be of semi balance spade type. A suitable rudder bulb shall be fitted on the rudder.

The rudder area to be designed as per Class rules.

Propeller shall be capable of removal without dismantling the rudder ,rudder bulb.

The rudder plates and horizontal & vertical rudder frames to be of fabricated steel plate.

The rudder blade is made of high quality, sand blast shipbuilding steel and is pressure tested.

The rudder blade is constructed with a streamline cone coupling for the connection to the rudder stock.

The rudder blade has a protection against corrosion, which is inside solution and outside primer.

Rudder blade to be arranged with provision for hoisting eye.

Earthing device to be provided for rudder stock.

The jumping stopper shall be provided in way of the rudder top.

Rudder stock to be constructed of forged steel and to have keyless ways at the upper and lower ends to take steering gear and rudder respectively. Lower part of rudder stock to be tapered with screw, and connected with rudder by a nut. Rudder stock to be fitted with sleeve in way of lower bearing. ***Sleeves for rudder stock to be of stainless steel 316L material***

Lifting hole, lifting eye plate, air and drain plug of the rudder to be provided. ***Peep hole or small manhole shall be provided to take rudder pintle and bush clearance in afloat condition.***

### 4.2.3 BOWTHRUSTER

The bow thruster shall be provided as follows:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Location | Bow | |
| No. of set | One (1) | |
| Type | Tunnel type, CPP(Controllable Pitch Propeller) | |
| No. of blade | Four (4) | |
| Material of blade | Ni-Al-Bronze | |
| Prime mover | Type | Electric motor, IP23, single speed, squirrel cage ,non-reversible |
| Voltage | AC 440V, 60Hz, 3 phase |
| Insulation | F class |
| Capacity | Approx. 1,000kW input power |
| Rating | Thirty (30) minutes at rated capacity |
| Starting method | As per Maker’s recommendation | |
| Control | Start & stop | From the wheelhouse |
| Emergency stop | From bridge ***&*** wing console |
| Pitch control | From the bridge ***&*** wing console |

Bow thruster shall consist of propeller unit, electric motor control panel.

The electric motor shall be connected to the thruster unit through a coupling. The motor can be started/stopped from local starter and wheelhouse and can be stopped in emergency from both bridge wings. The running indication shall be provided in wheelhouse.

A suitable interlocking device shall be provided to prevent starting of driving motor unless vent fan is in operation.

Tunnel of bow thruster shall be fabricated by steel plate. A stainless steel (SUS 316) ring shall be installed inside the tunnel in way of the propeller blades for protection from cavitation.

The other material, accessories, spare parts and tools shall be provided in accordance with the Maker’s standard to comply with the Rule/Regulations.

Galvanized steel grid shall be provided at entrance of thruster tunnel according to Maker’s recommendation. The configuration and orientation of thruster tunnel grid shall be determined as per results of stream line paint test and Builder's standard.

Bow thruster room shall be ventilated by one (1) mechanical supply fan to remove the heat. The ventilation duct shall be arranged so that the air flow passes over the electric motor. Vent shall not be in a position where moist air could be drawn into the bow thruster motor space.

Electric heater for the bow thruster room shall be provided.

**Bilge high level alarm is to be fitted in the Bow thruster Room.**

**Bow thruster starter/control panel to be placed outside the bow thruster motor level.**

***A easily accessible hatch with lifting arrangements to be provided for lifting the Bow Thruster motor from the location to outside the forecastle space to be provided.***

## 4.3 CARGO HATCH COVER

The hatch cover to be provided as shown on the G.A. plan.

The hatch cover to be designed in accordance with the requirement of the Classification Society and to be equipped with necessary outfit and accessory.

The material, construction, designs, etc. of the hatch cover to be in accordance with the Maker’s standard subject to approval of the Classification Society.

### 4.3.1 CARGO HATCH

Cargo hatches shall be arranged as shown on the G.A. plan and opening size shall be as follows:

|  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Hatchway | Length  (Approx. mm) | Width  (Approx. mm) | No. of panels | Type | Tightness |
| No. 1 | 12,600 | 15,282 | 2 | Pontoon, Non-sequential | Weather- tight |
| No. 2 | 12,600 | 20,258 | 2 |
| No. 3 ~No.8 | 12,600 | 25,030 | 2 each |

### 4.3.2 CARGO HATCH cover

#### 4.3.2.1 Strength and Structure

The hatch cover shall be of single plated, welded open type steel construction. The hatch covers shall be fabricated with approved mild steel and/or higher tensile steel according to the manufacturer's practice.

Cargo hatch covers shall be designed according to Class rules ***and MO32 of AMSA***, and designed according as the followings:

1. Uniform load according to the requirements of Class and ICLL.
2. Design stack load

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | 20ft | 40ft |
| For hatch No.1 | 60 MT | 90 MT |
| For hatch No.2 ~No.8 | 90 MT | 120MT |
| Upper deck aft | 90 MT | 120MT |

The above stack load on hatch covers to be only as design basis of hatch cover strength, and the actual achievable stack load on hatch covers at specified positions shall be decided by lashing force calculations by the Maker.

For weather-tightness, hatch covers shall be fitted with rubber packing along the hatch periphery and double lips rubber seals or equivalent type for longitudinal panel joint in accordance with the manufacturer's standards. Water bar will be fitted on top plates along the longitudinal joints.

Maximum hoist weight of hatch cover panel (including fixed fittings but excluding all other container loose fittings) shall be about 35 MT.

Operation of panels to be non-sequence type operated by shore cranes.

The design condition of hatch cover operation shall be max. 2 degree of trim and 3 degree of heel.

#### 4.3.2.2 Fittings and Others

***Flexible pad type (replaceable) with laminated rubber bearing pad or equivalent shall be provided as per Maker's standard.***

The hatch cover panel shall be secured to the hatch coaming top plate by manual anti-lifting devices according to Maker’s standard.

Transverse/longitudinal pin stopper at forward of hatch panel and transverse stopper at aft of hatch panel shall be provided which shall be also used to serve the entry guide of covers.

When being opened, the hatch cover to be stacked on the top of other hatch cover up to three (3) panels as far as practicable.

When stacking, the stacking foot underneath the hatch cover to be rested on stacking foundation on top plate of the other hatch cover.

When stacking, sufficient height considering the container loose fitting (bottom twist lock) to be provided between each stacked panels.

Lifting sockets(8 pcs per panel) shall be fitted near the center of gravity of each panel for hatch cover handling by 20ft and 40ft spreader and eye plate(only for 20ft) . A doubling plate shall be provided around the lifting sockets.

ISO raised sockets on the hatch cover may be used as hatch cover lifting sockets, if possible.

Holding down device and jumping stopper shall be provided for the hatch cover.

Necessary marks such as name of hatch, bay number, row number and panel weight shall be marked with intermittent welded line and painted on each hatch cover.

The necessary ventilation for holds around hatch covers to be installed, if required.

Hatch cover handling test shall be carried out with each hatch cover to demonstrate the performance of the hatch cover guiding system and the hatch cover stacking system. This test can be combined with the installation of the hatch cover during construction of the Vessel.

## 4.4 CONTAINER lashing and securing

The Vessel to be designed for carrying ISO standard container of the types stated in Section 2.2 of “General Part” of the Specification.

Lashing and securing system shall ensure safe carriage of containers of all variations of high and low cube containers as per the requirement of Rules and Regulations.

Cargo Safe Access Plan (CSAP) in accordance with MSC.1/Circ.1352and MSC.1/Circ. 1353 to be prepared by the Builder.

All container loose fittings and Container Securing Manual (CSM) required by IMO shall be provided by the Buyer.

***The loose twist stackers supplied by the Buyer for mixed stowage shall be stowed in the***

***dedicated storage bins and racks supplied by the Buyer on upper deck***

### 4.4.1 CONTAINER arrangement

#### 4.4.1.1 Container Fittings in Hold

The container stowage and securing method in hold shall meet the requirement of OSHA.

Twin 20ft containers shall be loaded in the 40ft cell up to maximum five (5) tiers from tank top.

Fixed stacking cones shall be welded on the tank top with doubling plate at each corner of 40ft container, and guide fitting at 20ft ISO gap for supporting the containers against the shifting.

Regardless of the maximum designed stack weight for tank top strength, the stack weight and the weight distribution will follow the calculation results of Rules.

The transverse clearance between two adjacent rows container in hold to be about 50 mm, in general.

#### 4.4.1.2 Container Fittings on Deck and Hatch Cover

The container stowage on deck and hatch cover shall meet the requirement of CSS Code including MSC.1/Circ.1352.

Arrangement and number of containers on upper deck, hatch cover and container deck stanchion to be as shown on the G.A. plan.

45ft container (45’ x 8’ x 9’6”) could be stowed on hatch covers from 2ndtier above No.2~No.8 hatch without additional lashing as outlined on G.A. plan.

Container on hatch cover to be arranged as symmetrical as possible in the section view and the transverse clearance between containers to be about 38mmin general.

In general, the containers on hatch covers and upper deck shall be secured by the combined use of twist locks, lashing rods, turnbuckles, and lashing eyes.

Regardless of the maximum designed stack weight for the hatch covers and upper deck aft, the maximum achievable stack weight of containers, especially for the outmost row(s) containers, may be adjusted in accordance with the lashing calculation result as per Class Rule based on the following lashing patterns or lashing patterns by Maker’s recommendation.

Lashing pattern:

Internal lashing pattern shall be applied, in general.

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | For 40ft /45ft containers on hatch cover and upper deck | For 20ft containers | |
| Inboard container stacks | Double cross lashing (short) | Gap | single short cross |
| End | single short cross |
| Outboard container stacks | Double cross lashing (short) + Single diagonal lashing(long) | Gap | Single short cross+long wind lashing+long vertical lashing |
| End | double lashing |

Container lashing method shall be in accordance with the Maker’s standard to comply with the Rules requirement and shall be submitted to the Buyer for reference.

The permissible weight distribution of containers in each tier to be decided in accordance with the Class Rules.

The container fixed fitting to be arranged on hatch cover, deck stanchion and upper deck based on the above lashing patterns.

ISO raised type twist lock foundation (about 110 mm high) and fixed type lashing eye plate shall be fitted on hatch cover, deck stanchion and upper deck for container stowage. Eye plate shall be sufficiently spaced to allow for easy inserting /removal of lashing bar ends.

Elongated-hole type twist lock sockets shall be fitted on outmost side of hatch cover or on deck stanchion considering hatch cover movement as per Maker’s recommendation.

All loose lashing and securing fittings such as semi-automatic twist locks, lashing rods, turnbuckles etc., and Container Securing Manual (CSM) required by IMO shall be supplied by the Buyer.

### 4.4.2 Lashing bridge and reefer maintenance platform

No lashing bridge and reefer maintenance platforms to be provided on deck.

Two (2) sets of aluminum portable ladder to be provided for reefer container.

### 4.4.3 container DECK STANCHION and operation platform on weather deck

Containers stowed on the outermost sides shall be supported by hatch covers and container deck stanchions as shown on the G.A. plan.

Container deck stanchion shall be of fabricated box type steel construction, and shall be designed based on the same stack load as the hatch covers.

Vertical ladder or hand grips and steps to be provided for access from weather deck to top of the deck stanchion.

Fixed handrail to be provided where necessary.

***The deck stanchion shall be designed to ensure clear height of passage way from upper deck to bottom of first tier container on hatch cover to be min. 2,000 mm.*** ***Non-skid paint to be applied along the walkway with skirting of contrast color.***

Transverse working platform shall be provided between cargo hold: Width of clear passageway on working platform: 600mmin general. Height to beat the same level as the top of hatch covers.

Removable handrails and galvanized steel rope with vinyl coating on both side of working platform to be provided,

Access to working platform shall be provided through a vertical ladder from upper deck.

Reefer container socket to be fitted on the hatch coaming and weather protected (IP56)

### 4.4.4 Cellular Construction

Cellular construction shall be of fixed, continuous type and designed to guide and support the six(6) tiers of 8’6”standard containers.

The cell guide shall be reinforced to permit the stowage of 9’6” high cube container randomly in cargo hold in flexi loading condition.

The cell guides shall be of about 160 mm x 160 mm x 14 mm equal angle construction. The cell guides shall extend continuously from the entry guide down to around 2.0 meters above the inner bottom or container platforms in the cargo hold.

The top of each cell guide shall be connected to a fixed entry guide fabricated with ***22*** mm thickness steel plate, and the enter guides shall be of wave type in accordance with the Builder’s practice.

The cell guides and cell guide support structure shall be designed based on the container unit weight of 30.5MT per 20ft/40ft container. ***From entry guide within 2 meters the support bracket shall be double pieces to be installed (to be confirm at approved drawing).***

Side guide plates shall be provided in way of location between each 20ft container as follows:

For guide plate in way of side longitudinal bulkhead of all cargo hold:

(1) Approx. from hatch coaming top level to upper deck level

(2) Approx. 1.5m length above the tank top 1000m.

The side guide rails would be not fitted on other step bulkhead.

The test for container loading and unloading with real or dummy container shall be carried out in accordance with the Builder’s practice.

The bay numbers based on 40ft containers and row numbers shall be marked with Intermittent welding line and painted on the side/end wall of each cargo hold.

### 4.4.5 Others

Painted steel boxes or hangers for loose container fittings storage to be provided by the Buyer.

Turnbuckle shall always be secured by lashing eyes on hatch covers and deck stanchions if necessary and in accordance with the Maker’s standard.

Lashing bar storage provided by builder, other storage boxed are provided by Buyer.

## 4.5 CARGO GEAR

### 4.5.1 CARGO gear

No deck crane to be fitted.

## 4.6 LIFE SAVING APPLIANCE

The Vessel shall be provided with lifesaving and protection equipment for a complement of 24 persons and to comply with the requirement of the Rule/Regulations.

**Effective term of ten (10) months shall be available for all LSA and FFA certificates at the time of the Vessel’s delivery.**

### 4.6.1 LIFEBOAT WITH EQUIPMENT

The lifeboat shall be provided as follows:

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| No. of set | Two (2) |
| Type | Totally enclosed  Starboard side lifeboat shall be used as rescue boat. |
| Material | Glass reinforced plastics(GRP) |
| Capacity | 24persons |
| Propulsion | Diesel engine (sea water cooling) |
| Location | Beside deck house as shown on G.A. plan |

Dimension, capacity and certified date shall be marked at position approved by the Regulation.

Name of ship, Call sign, complement and port of registry shall be painted.

The boat embarkation area to be protected and illuminated sufficiently.

***Emergency lighting*** and instruction sheet (in English) shall be fitted on wall near the lifeboat.

Construction, material, and accessories shall be in accordance with the approved manufacturer’s standard to comply with the Rule/Regulations.

### 4.6.2 Lifeboat davit and winch

One (1) set of hinged gravity type davit to be provided at port and starboard side as shown on G.A. plan.

The davit to be made of fabricated steel and to be complete with necessary blocks, tackles and galvanized steel wire rope, etc.

One (1) set of electric motor driven winch shall be fitted for each lifeboat davit. Davit shall be capable of manual operation by handle in case of emergency. The winch to have sufficient capacity for lowering fully equipped life boat with persons on board to the ballast draft. ***One independent starter/control panels to be used for each life boat davit and winch.***

Each winch shall have two (2) limit switches to avoid over-hoisting.

Guide fittings (skate) for easily lowering the lifeboat shall be fitted. Lighting and instruction sheet (in English) shall be fitted on the wall near the lifeboat.

Other material, fittings, and construction not specified above shall be in accordance with the manufacturer’s standard in compliance with the Rule/Regulations.

The speed of starboard side winch of hoisting speed to be in accordance with the requirements for rescue boat. The designated rescue boat davit shall be capable for the lifeboat recovery within 5 minutes as per SOLAS requirements.

### 4.6.3 LIFE RAFT AND DAVIT

4.6.3.1 Life Raft

Life rafts shall be provided as follow:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| No. | Capacity (persons) | Type | Position |
| 1 | 24 | Inflatable, throw overboard type with a hydrostatic releasing device | Accommodation port side |
| 1 | 24 | Inflatable, throw overboard type with a hydrostatic releasing device | Accommodation starboard side |
| 2 | 6 | Inflatable, throw overboard type | Ship’s forward |

Each one (1) embarkation ladder shall be supplied for liferaft at accommodation port side and starboard side.

Two (2) embarkation ladders shall be arranged at the protected location on forward ship.

The canvas covers for these ladders to be provided.

The inflatable life rafts shall be stowed in fiber glass reinforced plastic (FRP) container. The container shall be stowed in cradle and float free,

Effective term of nine (9) months shall be available for the life rafts at the time of the Vessel’s delivery.

Indication lamp and instruction sheet (in English) shall be provided for life raft.

4.6.3.2 Life Raft Davit

Life raft davit shall not be provided.

### 4.6.4 PERSONNEL LIFESAVINGS

Personnel lifesaving appliances shall be provided by the Builder in accordance with the Rule/Regulations of Classification Society and Flag Authority.

***Owner supply the SCBA and EEBD recharging compressor. Ship yard supply socket for the compressor,***

4.6.4.1 Life Jackets and Immersion Suits

Life jackets and immersion suits shall be provided for 24persons and stowed in each cabin in accordance with the Regulations.

Each life jacket shall be colored orange and marked with the name of the vessel and port of registry.

For other spaces, additional life jackets and immersion suits shall be provided and stowed, according to requirement of Classification Society and Flag Authority.

4.6.4.2 Lifebuoy

Lifebuoy shall be provided as per rules, general will be as follow:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Location | No. | Accessory |
| Vessel’s side (port and starboard) and stern rail | as per rule | Buoyant lifeline of about 30 m |
| Pilot boarding area | 2 | Self-igniting light |
| Near lifeboat and rescue boat | 2 | Self-igniting light |
| Near accommodation ladder | 2 | Self-igniting light and buoyant life line of about 30m |
| Navigation bridge deck (port and starboard) | 2 | Self-igniting light and self-activating smoke signal with quick releasing device |

The self-igniting light shall be kept near the lifebuoy to which it belongs.

The self-activating smoke signal shall be capable of producing smoke of highly visible color for at least 15 minutes.

Each of the lifebuoy shall be marked with the name of the Vessel and port of registry in black letters.

Lifebuoy shall be made of rigid polyurethane with plastic cover and fitted with grab line.

4.6.4.3 Lifeline Throwing Appliance

One (1) lifeline throwing appliance consisting of four (4) projectiles with four (4) lifelines shall be provided.

Each projectile shall be capable of carrying the line at least 230 m in calm weather.

4.6.4.4 Distress Flares

Twelve (12) sets of rocket parachute flares shall be provided.

### 4.7.3 FORE MAST, RADAR MAST, FORE AND STERN FLAG STAFF

Fore mast to be of fabricated steel construction, and to be arranged on the forecastle deck at the center line of the Vessel.

The fore mast to be furnished with vertical ladders, back hoop, mast light. Necessary fittings and eye plates for steel wire rope stays to be fitted to minimize vibration.

Radar mast to be of fabricated steel and to be arranged on the compass deck at the center line of the Vessel.

The radar mast shall be connected with under deck structure effectively and fastened by rigging and tackles to minimize vibration.

The radar mast to be furnished with vertical ladder, back hook, radar scanner, antenna fittings, mast light, signal yard, signal lamp. Necessary fittings and eye plates for steel wire rope stays to be fitted to minimize vibration.

Antenna post to be of steel pipe construction of self -standing type.

Necessary rigging and tackles for davits, flag yards, signal yard, etc. to be furnished completely.

All riggings to be greased before delivery and covered with vinyl cover.

One (1) ensign staff to be fitted at stern and one (1) jack staff at bow. And anchor lamp to be provided. Rigging to be fitted for flag staff completely.

One (1) flag box to be place around the fore and stern flag staff.

**Cables installed on mast or post on upper deck to be wired in galvanized steel pipe up to about 300mm height from the deck.**

* Winch drum of accommodation ladder and pilot assistant ladder

* Embarkation rope ladder for liferaft

## 4.8 outfitting for access

### 4.8.1 access HATCH, MANHOLEcover and steel door

#### 4.8.1.1 Access Hatch Cover, Rope Hatch Cover, etc.

Hatches for access, etc. shall be provided to the space listed in the table hereinafter. Nuts, bolts for hatches on weather deck shall be of stainless steel SUS304.

The coaming height shall be complied with ICLL requirement and all weather-tight doors and hatches shall be tested according to class approved method..

All hatches except those specially indicated shall be of hinged type.

Number and size of hatches for each compartment to be as follows:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Served Space | Number | Size (mm) |

2. All hatches shall have eye plates for pad lock (except escape hole).

#### 4.8.1.2 Manhole Cover and Other Bolted Cover

Oil tight or water tight oval manhole cover to be provided for double bottom tank, side tanks, cofferdams.

The manhole cover to be of steel and watertight or oil tight construction with synthetic rubber sheet gasket, bolts and nuts. Studs and nuts to be stainless steelSUS304, but those on exposed deck to be SUS316.The manhole cover to be of flush type on container stowage position in cargo hold and on under deck passageway floor. However on the tank top in engine room and oil tank, steel coaming of about 100 mm in height to be fitted.

In general, at least two (2) manhole covers shall be provided for each big tank with capacity over 20m3.

The manhole cover on wall to be fitted with handle.

The marks to be of welding line on the manhole cover, no additional mark on tank bulkhead. Steps and handles to be provided on vertical fitted manhole covers if the distance from lower edge of manhole to deck is more than 600 mm.

Number and size of manhole cover and bolted cover for each space to be as follows:

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Served Space | Size (mm) |
| Oil tank | 400 x 600 (oval) |
| Fresh water tank | 400 x 600 (oval) |

| Chain locker (on chain locker wall in bosun store) | 600 x 800 (hinged) |
| Ballast water tank | 400 x 600 (oval) |
| Other hull structure tanks in E/R | 400 x 600 (oval) |
| Cofferdam and void space | 400 x 600 (oval) |
| Pipe duct | 400 x 600 (oval) |
| Stern tube cooling water tank | 400 x 600 (oval) |

### 4.8.2 steel ladder and HAND RAIL

#### 4.8.2.1 Access Ladder on Deck, in Cargo Hold / Tank etc.

Access ladders shall be provided as follows:

| Served space | Type | Breadth (mm) | Side stringer | Tread | Handrail |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

| Other exposed deck |

| Cargo hold | Vertical | 350 | Steel flat bar | Steel square bar, 22x22mm | -- |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| Fuel oil bunker tank, Ballast water tank, F.W. tank, E/R escape, funnel, bow thruster room, access trunk, deck stanchion | Vert. | 350 | Steel flat bar | Steel square bar 22mm,  pitch: abt.300mm | Round bar, 25mm dia. where necessary |
| Mast, post, miscellaneous part | Vert. | 300 | Steel flat bar | Steel square bar 22mm  pitch: abt.300mm | Round bar, 25mm dia. where necessary |

In general, ladder breadth shall be 350 mm and in no case not less than 300mm, middle support to be used for ladder length more than 2.5m***.Ladder safety hoop will be install according to AMSA rules.***

Non-slip paint to be taken at landing area from exposed deck to ladder.

Hand grips and steps to be provided, where necessary.

Ladder and handrail in ballast water tank and exposed to weather to be galvanized and to be painted as surrounding area.

Elevation angle of inclined ladder to be 55 deg. (max. 60 deg. In E/R and max. 65 deg. In cargo hold) to horizontal. But the elevation angle of inclined ladder used as means of escape to be not greater than 50 deg. To horizontal. Hand rail of inclined ladder to be fitted on each side.

**Mid Rail should be provided for incline ladders and the rail if the distance of the top railing from the step base is equal to or more than 500 mm in height.**

***All ladders and railing stanchions when welded to decks should be done with a doubler plate.***

#### 4.8.2.2 Hand Rail on Exposed Deck

The maximum distance of the rail stanchion, hand rail shall comply with Rules.

The height from hand rail top to deck shall be abt. 1,050mm, in general.

Handrails of Ø 42.25x 3.25 mm outer diameter top pipe (galvanized water gas pipe) and 0ne(1) Ø 20 mm steel round bars lower rails shall be fitted for exposed decks. Stanchion shall be 60 mm x16 mm flat bar with stay. Stanchion for masts, posts and platforms etc. on exposed deck shall be 60 mm x 16 mm flat bar without stay.

Stanchions shall be be welded with pad and welded to the curtain plate or deck and shall be well withstood to ensure rigidity of rail.

The stanchion shall be provided at about 1,500 mm intervals in general and the stay at every third stanchion, if fitted.

Non-magnetic hand rail shall be used in way of the compass on wheelhouse top shall be as per Maker's requirement.

**Gap between handrail and bulkhead/fittings shall be minimum 60 mm.**

#### 4.8.2.3 Hand Rail in Cargo Hold

The maximum distance of the rail stanchion, hand rail shall comply with Rules.

The height from hand rail top to deck shall be abt. 1,050 mm, in general, ***mid rails will be provided.***

Handrails of Ø 42.25x 3.25mm outer diameter top pipe (galvanized water gas pipe) and 0ne(1) Ø 20mm steel round bars lower rails shall be fitted for stringer platform in cargo hold. Stanchion shall be 60 mm x16 mm flat bar without stay.

#### 4.8.2.4 Storm Rail

Galvanized storm rail of 42.25mm outside diameter steel pipe (galvanized water gas pipe) to be fitted on outside wall of deckhouse where persons frequently walk around and to be positioned at about 1,000 mm above deck with adequate distance from the wall.

***Removable life lines and stanchions should be provided between accommodation front and forecastle deck as Rule's requirement where the width of clear passageway is more than 1.2m.***

## 4.9 SPARE PART AND DECK INVENTORY

Spare parts, tools and inventory shall be furnished as per the Maker's and/or Builder's practice in accordance with the Rules recommendation of the Classification Society unless otherwise specifically described in this Specification.

**2 -** Thermometer for atmosphere (dry and wet)

1 - Hand lead, 3.2kg weight with 55 meters line

1 - Chronometer, portable type (battery use)

1 - Sextant

2 - Clinometer (small clock type in wheelhouse and E/R)

1 - Clinometer (in ship office)

**Hygrometer and Barometer should have calibration certificates.**

Electric navigation instrument such as gyro compass, radar, echo sounder, velocity-meter, clock, etc. shall refer to "Part IX –Electric Part".

# CHAPTER 5 HULL PIPING

## 5.1 HULL PIPING

### 5.1.1 GENERAL

Description of this section shall generally cover piping system located outside the engine room, unless otherwise specified.

Materials and dimensions of pipes, joints, valves including bolts, nuts, etc. shall be manufactured in accordance with the Chinese Industrial Standard, and/or the Builder’s Standard except otherwise specified hereinafter, the diameter of connecting flange and distance between flanges of valves shall be in accordance with ISO standard.

The other recognized industrial standards than mentioned above may be applied to meet the requirements of the Classification Society.

Valves, pipes and fittings mounted on its equipment shall be in accordance with the manufacturer’s standard.

All overboard discharges shall be kept clear of pilot ladder, accommodation ladder, draft marking, load line marking and lifeboat launching area as far as practical.

Piping shall be designed to allow for stress due to thermal expansion and deflection of the Vessel’s structure.

No ballast pipes or vents for ballast tanks shall pass through oil tanks or vice versa, in general.

### 5.1.2 PIPING MATERIAL AND WORK

5.1.2.1 Pipe

The materials and wall thickness of pipes shall be in accordance with “Table of pipes” of this section and to meet the requirements of the Classification Society.

The pipes as a part of machinery or equipment supplied by the manufacturer in package shall be of the manufacturer’s standard.

Pipe bore shall be decided so as to accommodate given flow quantity and corresponding pump pressure.

Pipe lines shall be led with a minimum number of bends and the arrangements shall avoid well part where drains likely to stay as far as practical.

Suitable draining shall be provided for the well parts of water pipes in exposed locations where those may be frozen.

Liquid pipes shall be kept away from switchboard and the electrical appliances. Where the piping is unavoidably led above the electrical appliances (other than MSB, G/Es, transformers etc.), the welded sleeve joint shall be provided.

Where the pipe lines pass through girders or any other structural elements, the compensation shall be provided in accordance with the requirements of the Classification Society and Builder’s standard if necessary

The bend radius of pipe shall be not less than 2.5 times outside diameter, except elbow.

For flushing of the pipe, refer to the “Chapter 6 Machinery” of the Specification.

5.1.2.2 Valves

In general, the valve side shall be of the same nominal bore as that of the pipes connected except automatic control valves.

In general, for DN80mm and above. butterfly valves will be used as far as possible. Such as high pressure and high temperature system to be excepted. Butterfly valves to be wafer type with NBR/ Viton liner and bronze/stainless steel disc except shipside valves.Shipside butterfly valves to be double flange type. ***Some of wafer type may be changed into lug type, it will discuss in detail design stage between the Owner and yard.***

Use of gate valves shall be limited where require by Classification Society for the purpose of fire protecting closure.

Cast steel and ductile cast iron valves shall be fitted to such locations as required by the Classification Society.

Installation of the ship side valve shall be in accordance with the requirements of the Classification Society and shall be fitted rigidly to the shell with short stub piece of heavy wall (as per Rule requirement) as far as practicable.

Generally the actuators of remote butterfly valves shall be of enclosed double acting type, single acting type to be used according to the requirement of class and shall be directly coupled to the valves.

Remote control valves shall be provided with local manual operation device required by Classification Society.

Valve name plates of brass or stainless steel shall be fitted to the valves on handle or other suitable place.

5.1.2.3 Pipe Jointing

In general, the welded sleeve joints, butt welding and flange connection shall be applied to steel pipe, joints, fittings, machinery and where necessary according to the Builder’s practice.

Pipe joint of ballast system and bilge system shall be of flange type as far as possible. The material of pipe connection shall be of the same material or similar to that of the pipes connected, unless otherwise specified.

In general, flange joint shall be of steel fillet weld-on type for steel piping

Preformed welding socket shall be used for high pressure steel pipe such as hydraulic oil line, etc.

Butt welding joint shall be applied for reducer, elbow, tee, and others except otherwise specified.

Galvanized steel hexagonal head bolts and nuts shall be used for piping in ballast water tank, weather deck, etc.

Metric threaded and/or welded type unions may be used at dismantling point of small bore steel pipe or non-ferrous tubes.

For copper or aluminum brass piping, braze union or bite joint or sleeve shall be applied for small bore pipes and screw union for large bore pipes.

***U bends, where not practical the joint must be inspected prior fitting the sliding coupling by owner’s site team, such as ballast water pipe and bilge pipes in pipe duct,*** shall be generally used for ballast, bilge, fire main, cable protection lines, etc., where necessary, to compensate for the pipes expansion and contraction.

Offset expansion bends (Loop) shall be applied to compressed air line, steam line, high pressure hydraulic oil lines and wherever practicable.

5.1.2.4 Bulkhead and Deck Penetrations

Where the pipe lines pass through the watertight or oil tight bulkheads and decks, the bulkhead or deck shall be sufficiently compensated, where necessary, in accordance with the requirements of the Classification Society.

The standard penetration pieces shall be complied with class requirement.

The connections through the insulated bulkheads shall be of suitable length to permit access to flange connections without disturbing the insulations.

Full penetration at the side shell welding and inspection shall be performed according to rule and standards.

5.1.2.5 Tees, Bends, and Other Fittings Etc.

Branch pipes for low pressure piping up to 5MPa shall be welded directly to the main pipe.

For high pressure pipes of DN40 mm and below, socket welding type tee shall be used. Standard elbow pieces and reducers shall be of fabricated steel made by electric arc welding.

Fittings forming a part of pipe shall be of the equivalent material as jointing pipes in general.

As a standard for steel and non-ferrous pipes, pipe bending shall be carried out by means of cold bending machine, to maximum practicable according to the Builder’s facility.

If cold bending is not applicable or small bending radius is necessary to facilitate the piping arrangement, high frequency induction bending or butt-welding elbow shall be used.

The loose fittings (Filters, Strainers, Traps, Rose Box, Mud Box, Rose Plates, Plugs, Nozzles, Orifice, expansion couplings, separators, air pipe heads, etc.) shall be selected by pipe size, line pressure and pipe line material according to Builder’s practice.

5.1.2.6 Suction Bell Mouth

Inverted hopper shape suction bell mouth fabricated of mild steel shall be used in general,.

Double plate shall be installed below bell mouths (10mm).

The clearance between suction bell mouth and tank bottom shall be Builder's standard.

5.1.2.7 Gasket and Packing

Universal heat and oil resistant asbestos free gaskets shall be used for all piping system.

The type of gasket shall be ring type, and the thickness of gasket used shall be according to Builder’s practice.

Material of packing for valve stem shall be of valve maker’s standard.

5.1.2.8 Pipe Supports

The piping shall be securely supported by steel angle with clamping methods to avoid damage, vibrations and movement in accordance with the Builder’s practice.

PE/Copper Pipe Makers standard to be followed in systems where the material is utilized.

Pipe supports for non-ferrous pipe shall be lined with sliding pad of copper, brass, plastic or synthetic rubber so as to not to directly contacted with pipes.

All pipe supports and on deck as well as inside water tanks to be of hot-dip galvanized material.

Fixing supports shall be provided for preventing floated pipe from excessive free moving, where required.

For clamping, “U” shape steel round bar bolt clips shall be used for steel pipes (DN≥15mm) and Maker’s standard to be applied for the others. ***All U clamps on Deck and Ballast tanks to be of stainless steel. Steam pipe, condensate pipe and copper line to be installed with Teflon or equivalent pads at bottom and top to avoid metal to metal contact with the pipes.***

In general, double nuts U-bolts shall be used for all heating coils (each one on both sides of the support).

However, all size of vent pipes, and the other pipes not mentioned above shall be supported according to shipyard standard.

Heating coils pipes and others subject of temperature expansion to be provided with sliding pads or other means to compensate expansion.

Sliding pads shall be inserted between pipes and supports for the following pipes:

- Longitudinal pipes of ND125 mm and above in pipe duct

5.1.2.9 Pipe Protection

The piping works shall be protected from mechanical damage, where necessary and the protection shall be constructed with steel angels, plates or channels as per Builder’s practice.

5.1.2.10 Surface Treatment and Cleaning

The surface treatment and coating of the machinery, loose fittings and valves shall be carried out in accordance with builder's standard for the intended purpose, and no special surface treatment shall be made exceeding Maker’s standard unless otherwise specified.

The pipe fittings whose function is to join branches of the system (such as tees, Y-pieces, elbows, flanges, unions, bushing, etc.) shall be painted same as connected pieces.

The loose fittings other than above pipe fittings supplied by makers (such as expansion coupling, filters, strainers, traps, separator, rose boxes, nozzles, plug, orifice etc.) shall be painted in accordance with maker’s standard unless otherwise specified.

The galvanizing shall be carried out after fabrication of pipes in principle, but if welding has to be carried out after galvanizing for the cases mentioned below, the external surface of the damaged parts shall be touched up with two (2) coats of zinc solution paint of high purity.

a) Welded sleeve joints fabricated on-board

b) Flanges of pipes adjusted on-board

c) Middle flanges of penetrating pieces adjusted on -board

d) Butt wild joint adjusted on-board

The fuel oil service pipes, lubricating oil pipes and hydraulic oil pipes shall be pickled before installation, refer to Machinery Chapter paragraph 6.10.1of the Specification.

5.1.2.11 Inspection and Test

All the tests and inspections of pipe lines shall be carried out in accordance with the requirements specified in the specification and the Rules and Regulations and the Builder’s standard.

Visual Test

Dimensions, scantlings, locations, surfaces finishing, welding, fastenings, joints, etc. shall be visually inspected where necessary.

Leakage Test (Flow Test)

The pipes which to be occasionally filled up by gravity or pipes through which liquid flow without pressure during the actual service shall be tested by free flow of water to confirm tightness of pipe lines.

Pressure Test

The statically hydraulic pressure test shall be carried out in accordance with the requirement of the Classification Society.

During the pressure test, a blank flange shall be provided at the open ends with the valves and/or any other means of closing on the piping fully open. For pipe insulation refer to Machinery Chapter, item 6.9 of the Specification.

### 5.1.3 BILGE PIPING

Cargo hold

One (1) main bilge line for cargo holds shall be arranged in pipe duct and branched to each bilge well, fitted with rose box, non-return valve and remote control butterfly valve(arranged in pipe duct) at each suction mouth.

Each cargo hold shall have two (2) bilge wells at the aft end of the hold (one on each side of the Vessel).

The main bilge line shall be connected to fire, bilge & G.S pumps in engine room.

Dangerous goods bilge water in cargo holds shall be discharged overboard through the main bilge line by a dangerous goods bilge eductor located outside of the engine room when carry dangerous goods.

The bilge system shall be so designed that the dangerous goods can be carried in No.1~3 cargos holds. Shut off valve should be fitted directly at the bulkhead on machinery space of end of bilge main line to ensure the separation of bilge water from engine room when dangerous goods are loaded in cargo hold.

Bow part

One (1) bilge eductor shall be provided to discharge bilge in the chain locker, void space above fore peak tank and bosun store. And driving water for eductor shall be supplied from the fire main line.

One (1) bilge eductor shall be provided to discharge bilge in the bow thruster & emergency fire pump room. And driving water for eductor shall be supplied from the fire main line.

Stern part

Bilge water in the steering gear room shall be led to the bilge well in the engine room through self-closing valve.

Other spaces

The daily bilge piping system in E/R shall be independent of main bilge piping system.

Oily bilge discharge pipe with stop valve and MARPOL shore connection flange shall be provided at each side on upper deck.

The valve for bilge lines in engine room shall be manually operated.

For bilge pump and bilge system in the engine room, refer to the Machinery Specifications.

High level alarm shall be provided for bilge wells.

### 5.1.4 BALLAST PIPING

One (1) ballast main ring line shall be arranged in pipe duct for ballasting, de-ballasting and transferring the ballast water in double bottom ballast tanks, side ballast tanks.

Ballast system shall consist of two (2) ballast pumps and one (1) ballast water treatment plant in engine room.

Trim adjustment shall be remotely done by ballast system from ship office.

A suction bell mouth shall be provided in each ballast tank. The suction mouth shall be connected with flange in tanks and easily dismounted.

Drain hole shall be provided enough at structure member surrounding mouth pieces.

The remote control pneumatic butterfly valve shall be fitted on each branch ballast line in pipe duct and shall be remote operated from ship office.

All remote operated ballast water valves can be open/shut manually in case failure of remote operation. And local open/shut indication shall be provided for the remote operated ballast water valves.

The valve before collision bulkhead shall be fitted directly at the collision bulkhead inside the bow thruster & emergency fire pump room located after the collision bulkhead, the valve operation position as per Class Rules.

Remote level able to display tank volumes and draft reading for ballast tanks shall be indicated on monitor in ship office and loading computer.

Particulars of ballast pumps and remote control butterfly valve system refer to Machinery Chapter of the specification.

### 5.1.5 ANTI-HEELING PIPing

Two (2) anti-heeling tanks (P&S) shall be cross connected by steel pipes and one (1) dedicated anti-heeling pump shall be provided.

During loading and unloading of containers, heel adjustments shall be carried out by means of transferring the sea water between one pair of side ballast tank (port and starboard).

The anti-heeling operation shall be effected by start and stop sequence of heeling pump and respective control of valve and shall be controlled the Vessel's heel within +/-2 degrees.

Heeling control system shall have the start/stop function for heel adjusting, the heel indication and the over heeling alarm for heel adjusting tanks on the heeling control mode on TFT in ship office.

Before loading and unloading of containers, both anti-heeling tanks shall be about half filled with sea water.

Anti-heeling Pump

No. of set : One (1)

Capacity : About 350 m3/h x 15 mTH (according to final calculation)

Type : Reversible propeller type

Prime mover : Electric motor

Materials : Pump casing of bronze, impeller of Ni-Al-bronze and shaft of stainless steel

The following alarm shall be provided visible on the display of the operator panel and audible at the remote control panel:

Excessive Heeling (>5 degree)/ Emergency stop

Failure heeling pump and relative valves

Heeling tanks level alarm

The effect at any alarm occurring shall result in closing of valves and stopping of pump.

System common abnormal alarm to AMS shall be provided

### 5.1.6 VALVE REMOTE CONTROL SYSTEM

1) Valve remote operation

The valve control system of pneumatic type shall be provided for the remote control of following valves:

- Ballast valves in cargo hold area and major valves in engine room for ballast system

- Bilge suction valves in cargo hold area

- Fuel oil filling / suction main valves in cargo hold area

Discharge main valves of the ballast pumps shall have open, closed and intermediated position indications. Other valves shall have open and closed indication only.

The remote operated suction valves for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO bunker tanks in cargo hold area shall be single acting type.

The remotely controlled valves shall have an emergency operation facility by means of portable hand pump or spanner.

**Remote valves should not be placed in areas they serve and should be easily accessible in any operational condition of vessel. where is possible.**

2) Control

A control station with color graphic monitor shall be provided in the ship office, engine control room for ballast, bilge, FO.

Control functions and indications mentioned below shall be mounted on the monitor.

- Mimic diagram of ballast, bilge and FO system

- Open / shut function with indication for remote operated valves (Remote control valves in fuel oil system shall be controlled from engine control room.)

- Start/ stop function with running indication for ballast pump, fire, bilge & G.S. pumps.

- Suction and discharge pressure indication on monitor for ballast pump

- Level indication able to display tank volumes on monitor for water ballast, fresh water tank, HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO storage tanks and MGO storage tank.

- Draft indication on monitor

- High level alarm for cargo hold bilge wells, bosun store, fore & aft end of pipe duct, bow thruster & emergency fire pump room.

- Other necessary equipment and fittings not mentioned above shall be provided as per maker's standard

- HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO and MGO storage tanks shall be provided with independent level switches for high level alarm.

### 5.1.7 AIR AND SOUNDING PIPES

5.1.7.1 Air escape/Overflow Pipe

The air pipes shall be arranged in compliance with the load line regulation.

In general, one (1) or two (2) air pipes shall be provided for each tank and void space and shall be led to above exposed deck.

Air escape/overflow pipes shall be provided to all cofferdams and tanks, and shall be terminated in the place that shall be in accordance to the requirements of the classification society with suitable heads.

The air pipe head for fuel oil tank shall be fitted with float type closer and fire proof screen of stainless steel, and the head for fresh water tank shall be fitted with closer and stainless steel wire gauge insect guard. Air escape/overflow pipes for oil tanks shall be of steel and for other tanks shall be of steel pipe galvanized.

Oil spill coaming with plug shall be provided around air escape pipe head of oil tanks in accordance with the U.S.C.G. requirements.

Size of air escape/overflow pipes shall be not less than 125% of sectional area of suction pipe in accordance with the requirements of the Classification Society.

Air vent pipes for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO bunker tanks shall not be arranged passing through the water ballast tanks or vice versa as far as practicable.

The location of air vent head for fuel oil tanks shall be as per Rule’s requirement.

Welded sleeve joint shall be used for air escape pipe passing through deck.

Steel vent pipes to be required for water tanks outside of engine room.

5.1.7.2 Sounding Pipe

Sounding pipe with bronze screw type cap (deck stand type) or deck flush type shall be fitted to water ballast tanks, cofferdams and chain lockers, and terminated above upper deck or hatch coaming platform in accessible location.

Double bottom tanks in engine room shall be provided with short sounding pipe terminated above floor plating about 800 mm with self-closing devices, and self-closing test valves **are only used for double bottom oil or oily tanks in engine room according to class requirement.**.

The sounding pipes for side ballast water tanks shall be terminated on weather deck level. Those for double bottom ballast tanks and cargo hold bilge wells shall be arranged between transverse bulkhead and cell guide in cargo holds, and terminated on weather deck level.

The sounding pipes for HFO and ULSFO/LSHFO tanks shall be terminated on weather deck level in accessible location.

The sounding pipe shall be of steel pipe of 50 mm for fuel oil tanks and cargo hold bilge wells, 40 mm for water tank and chain locker unless otherwise required by the Class. Application of galvanization for sounding pipes shall be the same as air escape/overflow pipes.

Generally the sounding pipe shall be as straight as practicable and fitted with brass cap.

The lower end shall be extended to a height of about 20 mm above the tank bottom and striking pad of 10 mm thick shall be fitted to pipe end.

Lower part of sounding pipes about 350 mm length shall be detachable for removing broken sounding tapes.

One (1) test cock with self-closing valve shall be provided for stern tube cooling water tank.

Two (2) sounding tapes with plumb shall be furnished, one (1) for clean water tanks and the other for dirty oil tanks.

Sounding pipes for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO bunker tanks shall not be arranged passing through the water ballast tanks or vice versa as far as practicable.

***100mm coaming to be provided for all the sounding pipes used for oil tanks.***

***Ship side pipes/ Scuppers shall be welded to side shell with deep penetration weld.***

5.1.7.3 Remote Reading Level Gauge and Bilge Alarm

One (1) remote reading leveland volumegauge of electronic pressure sensor type able to display tank volumes shall be provided for each water ballast tank and fresh water tank.

One (1) remote reading level and volume gauge of electronic pressure sensor type able to display tank volumes shall be provided for each HFO , LSHFO/ULSFO and MGO tank as specified at Machinery Chapter 6.2.18.

High level alarm shall also be provided for HFO , LSHFO/ULSFO and MGO tank in engine room as specified at Machinery Chapter 6.2.18..

One (1) bilge high level alarm by a float switch shall be provided for each bilge well in all cargo holds, bosun store, , bow thruster & emergency fire pump room and fore end of pipe duct and one (1) common audible alarm for bilge wells shall be provided in engine control room and wheelhouse.

Suitable protection pipe for oil tank for electrical sensors cable submerged in tank shall be provided accordance with Maker’s recommendation. **PVC protection pipe to be used for water tanks and bolt(if used) to be stainless steel.**

5.1.7.4 Name plate

Name plates for air and sound pipes shall be provided in English.

### 5.1.8 FRESH WATER SERVICE SYSTEM

5.1.8.1 Cold fresh water system and technical water system

One (1) filling pipe shall be provided for fresh water tanks. And pipe inside of F.W. tank shall be seamless steel pipe.

Diameter of fresh water filling pipe shall be not less than 65mm.

Hydrophore tank system shall be adopted to supply cold fresh water.

Cold fresh water system shall have a general fresh water service line, and one (1) fresh water hydrophone tank and two (2) fresh water pumps driven by electric motor.

One (1) of two (2) pumps shall serve as stand-by for the respective service line mentioned above.

The pumps shall suck from the fresh water tanks, and discharge through the stop check valves to hydrophone tank.

Generally, fresh water supplied from the fresh water hydrophore tank in the engine room to be led to, wash basins, showers, bath tub, laundries, hospital, sanitary water system by means of branches with shut-off valves at the main for each deck and service for engine room, front windows of wheelhouse and deck washing.

The fresh water hydrophore tank shall be constructed of stainless steel and finished completely with gauge glass, pressure gauge, relief valve, drain connection and connection from the compressed air system for charging purpose.

The automatic pressure control shall be fitted to start and stop the pumps to maintain the necessary pressure in the tank.

5.1.8.2 Hot fresh water system

The closed loop system shall be adopted to supply hot fresh water and to consist of one (1) calorifier for heating water, one (1) hot water circulating pump, main circulating pipe and branch pipes.

The calorifier shall be shell& tube type which using steam &electric heating.

The system shall be supplied through non-return valve from fresh water hydrophore tank, and hot water shall be led to galley, pantries, wash basins, showers, bath tub, laundries, and lobby of refrigerated provision chamber, etc.

Hot water and cold water shall be also supplied to wheelhouse for front windows washing.

5.1.8.3 Distilled water system

The distilled water from the fresh water generator shall be passing through water meter and salinity indicator to the fresh water tanks.

5.1.8.4 Drinking water system

Drinking water line to be leaded from the fresh water hydrophore.

One (1) set of F.W. sterilizer and one (1) set of F.W. mineralizing unit to be provided for drinking water system.

The drinking water only led to galley, pantry and drinking water fountains.

5.1.8.5 Sanitary Water System

Grey water discharge pipe shall be led overboard independently of sewage pipe through one (1) storm valve above the light ballast water line and to the sewage holding tank.

Grey water shall include the discharged water from wash basin, small wash basin, sink, shower and bath tube.

Black water main pipe from toilets and urinals in each board can be led to the sewage treatment plant installed in engine room during in harbor or directly be discharged overboard by-passing the sewage treatment plant through one (1) gate valve and one (1) non-return valve near the light ballast water line during at sea.

After the treatment plant, the sewage also can be discharged overboard at sea or to sewage holding tank in harbor duration, then using the sewage pump to discharge overboard at sea.

Black water and grey water pipe line from hospital shall be led independently to the sewage treatment plant.

***The sewage holding tank must be provided with a pipe all round on the top with perforation to clean and flush the tank with sea water.***

Sufficient scuppers shall be provided for galley, pantry, lavatories, refrigerated provision chambers, passages in living quarters and other enclosed spaces, wherever necessary***.***

### 5.1.9 SCUPPER AND DRAINAGE SYSTEM

Sufficient scuppers shall be provided for all decks, top of deck houses and other enclosed spaces, wherever necessary.

Drainage shall be arranged away from accommodation ladder, pilot ladder and life boat position.

Upper deck scuppers shall have \grids, a rubber plug shall be provided on the top of each scupper.

Separate scuppers for refrigerated space shall be with plugs.

Scupper pipes shall be led to the weather decks or overboard directly according to the situation.

Storm valves shall be fitted for necessary pipes as required by the Classification Society.

Water sealed traps shall be fitted to the refrigerated provision chambers.

Scuppers shall be arranged accessibly, and hard bending for galley scuppers and soil pipes shall be avoided as far as possible.

Gutter way in stainless steel shall be arranged on the deck of galley with scuppers on each corner. Fat trap shall be provided for galley scuppers.

Adequate cleaning plugs shall be fitted, wherever necessary.

Necessary drain plugs shall be fitted as required.

Drain pan shall be fitted frames.

Gutter bar shall be fitted along the inside deck house on each deck, finally according to the detail design.

Gutter bars shall be fitted around deck machinery, steering gear etc.

Drain pipe from funnel top to engine casing top shall be provided.

### 5.1.10 COMPRESSED AIR PIPE FOR DECK USE

Suitable number connection piece shall be provided on weather deck including deckhouse, mooring deck, etc for general service.

Connection piece with DN15mm hose valve and hose coupling (quick coupling type) shall be provided.

Air shall be supplied from deck service air reservoir in the engine room.

Compressed air shall be supplied for following space or equipment:

Bosun store

Steering gear room

Workshop

Bow thruster & Emergency fire pump room

CO2 room

Emergency generator room

Air conditioning room

Paint store

Forecastle deck

Upper deck at an interval of 30m between cargo holds

Each deck outside of living quarters P/S

The separate airline from main air reservoirs via two (2) reducing valves shall be supplied to air horn with locally open valve.

### 5.1.11 FUEL OIL PIPING

Fuel oil filling main lines of one (1) DN200 for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO and one(1) DN100 for MGO respectively with butterfly valve and blank flange shall be provided.

The remote control valve shall be fitted on branch fuel oil filling line of each HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO bunker tanks.

The main lines shall be connected to the fuel oil fill piping and fuel oil transfer pump in engine room.

Each one(1) bunker station for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO and MGO shall be provided at each side of the vessel on upper deck, and with sampling device, thermometer, butterfly valves blank flanges, pressure gauges, spill trays etc.

Oil spill spaces with drain plug shall be provided at F.O. filling stations.

Caution plate required by U.S.C.G. shall be fitted on bunker station and ship office.

Remote level reading for oil tanks shall be indicated in engine room.

High level alarms shall be provided for HFO/ULSFO bunker tanks and MDO/MGO bunker tank.

### 5.1.12 FUEL OIL TANK HEATING SYSTEM

A steam line for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO bunker tank heating and a drain line in side void space (P or S) shall be led from engine room to fuel oil bunker tanks and FO overflow tank.

Heating coils shall be of seamless steel and heating area ratio shall be 0.06m2/m3 for heavy fuel oil bunker tanks.

The steam shall be led from steam supply main line in void space through under deck to each HFO/ULSFO tank via a manually operated shut-off valve, and led back to drain main line in the void space through a steam trap/strainer and a shut-off valve .

Steam tracing shall be adopted for suction pipe of HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO line and steam tracing shall be insulated together with HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO suction main line.

***The remote temperature reading shall be provided for the HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO bunker tanks.***

### 5.1.13 DRAFT GAUGE

The sea valves for draft gauges shall be manually operated at local side.

Draft gauges shall be provided to read fore, midship (P/S) and aft draft with remote reading by analogue and digital display on TFT in ship office.
