## 6.11 PIPING SYSTEMS IN ENGINE ROOM

### 6.11.1 COOLING SEA WATER SYSTEM

The system shall consist of three (3) sets of main cooling S.W. pump, two (2) sets of sea chest, scrubber sea water pump, two (2) sets of central cooler and valves, fittings and pipes.

The three (3) main cooling sea water pumps shall be of same model. Two (2) sets shall be operated at normal sea going and the third shall be as stand-by. Each one of them can be used for harbor service.

Main cooling S.W. pumps shall take suction from sea through sea chests stop valves and strainers and discharge to central coolers, then overboard or recirculation to high sea chest in engine room.

Two strainers at outlets of sea chests to be provided, made of steel plates and the inside to be galvanized. The bucket to be made of SUS with a mesh size of 5 mm diameter.

The back washing piping and inserted filter for central coolers shall be arranged.

Pump outlets to have plate non return valve and butterfly shut off valves.

The condenser of F.W. generator shall be directly cooled by sea water.

### 6.11.2 COOLING FRESH WATER SYSTEM

The system shall consist of L.T. cooling F.W. circuit and H.T. cooling F.W. circuit. The L.T. cooling F.W. circuit includes three (3) sets of L.T. cooling F.W. pump, L.T. F.W. expansion tank, valves, fittings and pipes. The H.T. cooling F.W. circuit includes two (2) sets of M/E jacket cooling F.W. pump and one (1) set of M/E jacketcooling F.W. cooler, M/E H.T.F.W. expansion tank and accessories etc.

The three (3) L.T. cooling F.W. pumps shall be of same model. Two (2) sets shall be operated at normal sea going and the third shall be as stand-by. Each one of them can be used for harbor service.

The various consumers for L.T. circuit listed as follows:

(1) M/E air cooler

(2) M/E L.O. cooler

(3) M/E jacket cooling F*.* W. cooler

(4) G/E air coolers and L.O. coolers

(5) Main air compressor

(6) Intermediate shaft bearing

(7) Air conditioning plant

(8) Packaged air cooler for galley, ECR

(9) Ref. condensers

(10) Atmospheric condenser

(11) Sample cooler for boiler

(12) MGO cooler in M/E & G/E F. O. supply modular unit

The L.T. F.W. temperature at central cooler outlet shall be designed of 36℃. The H.T. fresh water shall be used for heating of F.W. generator.

The electronic type temperature regulating valves shall be provided for H.T. and L.T. fresh water circuits.

Feed water shall be auto supplied by float valve to M/E H.T. F.W. expansion tank and L.T. F.W. expansion tank from fresh water service system of the F.W. hydrophore tank.

One (1) set of M/E jacket F.W. pre-heater shall be provided in H.T. fresh water circuit, which capacity to be 1% of main engine SMCR.

G/E H.T. F.W. pre-heater unit shall be provided according to the manufacturer’s recommendation.

### 6.11.3 LUBRICATION OIL SYSTEM

#### 6.11.3.1 L.O. Filling and Transfer Systems

One (1) each separate deck filling lines with stop valve and blank flanges shall be arranged on bunker station port & stb side. for main engine and generator engine system oil. The main engine cylinder oil filling line shall be arranged on bunker station port & stb. side.

The lub. oil transfer pump shall be arranged to transfer L.O. between the lub. oil tanks in engine room or to discharge overboard via “on deck” filling connections.

A simplex filter shall be provided at suction side of lub. oil transfer pump.

#### 6.11.3.2 Lub. Oil Service System

Lubrication of the M/E main bearings, thrust bearings, bottom-end bearings, crosshead bearings, together with piston cooling, is carried out by the main lubricating oil system.

The lubricating oil pump shall draw from the lub. oil sump tank and through LO cooler, a thermostatic control valve and auto. back wash filter or a by-pass filter then enter to the main engine. Lubricating oil shall flow out directly from engine crankcase into the lub. oil sump tank after lubrication or piston cooling.

M/E turbocharger shall be lubricated from the main engine system oil.

The lub. oil sump tank shall be arranged in double bottom.

Cylinder oil from cylinder oil storage tank(s) shall be transferred to cylinder oil service tank by a pump ***and a high level auto cut off for the pump to be provided.***

Cylinder lubricating oil shall be fed to the main engine by means of a pump station mounted on the engine from the cylinder oil service tank.

Each generator engine shall have its own internal lubrication oil system with components built on the engine.

Lub. oil cooler shall have a thermostatic valve for temperature control. The return of the back flush filter shall be arranged close to the purifier suction and far from the main L.O. pump suction.

#### 6.11.3.3 L O. Purifying System

The main engine and the generator engines shall have independent L.O. purifying system.

The main engine L.O. purifying system shall have one (1) set ME L.O. purifier. Lub. oil purifier shall be connected so that purification may be carried out from the main engine lub. oil sump tank or the lub. oil settling tank to the lub. oil settling or the main engine sump tank.

The generator engines L.O. purifying system shall have one (1) set AE L.O. purifier. Lub. oil purifier shall be connected so that purification may be carried out from the G/E or the lub. oil settling tank to the lub. oil settling tank or G/E.

Sludge and water from the purifier shall be led to the sludge tank, and shall be shifted to waste oil tank for incinerator or to shore by the sludge pump.

#### 6.11.3.4 Lub. Oil Drain

Dirty oil collected from the M/E scavenge box is led to the M/E scavenge box drain tank and then to waste oil tank.

Save-all drip pans shall be provided for lub.oil pumps, purifiers and tanks, and shall be led to the waste oil rank.

### 6.11.4 FUEL SYSTEM

Fuel oil system including the equipment such as purifiers, F.O. supply unit, heating coils, etc. to be designed for operation with HFOof 380 cSt at 500C.

#### 6.11.4.1 Fuel Oil Filling and Transfer System

The FO filling line shall be led to the HFO , LSHFO/ULSFO bunker tank and MGO bunker tank.

Each FO filling connection shall be provided with shut off valve, blank flange, pressure gauge, thermometer and sample taking device

One safety valve for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO filling line to protect filling pipe shall be provided and to be connected to F.O. overflow tank. One safety valve with same function shall be provided for MGO filling line.

Overflow during filling shall be routed to overflow tank with a high level alarm.

One (1) sets of HFO/LSHFO/ULSFO transfer pump in the engine room shall be arranged to transfer HFO/LSHFO from bunker tanks to the engine room HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO settling tanks.

Automatic start/stop pumping signal of HFO *and LSHFO/ULSFO* settling tanks shall be provided for HFO/LSHFO/ULSFO transfer pump by level switches.

The HFO/LSHFO transfer pump shall have suction also from HFO/LSHFO service tanks.

One (1) set of MGO transfer pump in the engine room shall be arranged to transfer MGO from MGO bunker tank to MGO service tank.

A simplex filter shall be provided at the suction side of each transfer pumps.

***Manual changed over from LSHFO/ULSFO settling tank to HFO settling tank. And automatic start/stop pumping. Long time run stop function will be supplied.***

#### 6.11.4.2 Fuel Oil Service System

##### 6.11.4.2.1 Main Engine and Generator Engines System

One (1) common F.O. supply module unit shall be provided for main engine and generator engines. The unit consists of two (2) fuel oil supply pumps, two(2) fuel oil circulating pumps, two(2) fuel oil heaters, one(1) auto back flushing filter, one(1) viscosity control equipment, one(1) venting tank and etc.

Fuel oil supply pump shall draw fuel oil from the HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO service tank or MGO service tank through a strainer and then discharge to main engine through a flow-meter, F.O. circulating pumps, the heaters (for HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO) and an automatic back flush filter (to be installed on the hot side). The heaters shall be fitted with automatic regulating controller, governed by a viscometer. Excessive fuel oil from main engine shall be led to the fuel oil circulating pump suction side through a venting tank.

An emergency MGO pump shall be fitted in F.O. supply module unit for emergency use, the power source of the MGO pump shall be from emergency switchboard. And the emergency MGO supply line shall be separate from the main fuel oil line.

The automatic change-over device between HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO and MGO shall be arranged in the FO supply module.

##### 6.11.4.2.2 Composite Boiler

Two (2) sets of composite boiler FO supply pump shall be provided and arranged near the LSHFO/ULSFO service tank.

LSHFO/ULSFO for composite boiler shall be drawn from the LSHFO/ULSFO service tank by the composite boiler fuel oil supply pumps and discharge to the burner of the oil fired section.

A connection of MGO shall be fitted at the suction side of the supply pump for cold starting.

During Vessel in emission control area, boiler’s fuel oil supply pump shall draw ULSFO/MGO from ULSFO/MGO service tank.

One (1) F.O. volume flow meter shall be provided.

##### 6.11.4.3 Fuel Oil Purifying System

Two (2) sets of FO purifier shall be provided; one set of them shall be operated and the other as stand-by.

HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO after settled in the settling tank shall be drawn by the suction pump of fuel oil purifier and shall be delivered to the purifier through the fuel oil heater.

After purification, the clean oil shall be discharged into HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO service tank.

Overflow pipe from the bottom of the service tank back to settling tank shall be provided.

Sludge and water from purifier shall be discharged into the sludge tank for incinerator or to shore by the sludge pump.

#### 6.11.4.4 Fuel Oil System besides the above

For the waste oil incinerator, MGO transfer line from the incinerator MGO tank shall be provided.

#### 6.11.4.5 F.O. Drain

Save-all drip pans shall be provided for pumps, purifiers and tanks and shall be led to the fuel oil drain tank.

### 6.11.5 COMPRESSED AIR SYSTEM

Compressed air to be provided to the various services at the following pressure:

3 MPa : Main engine starting

Generator engine starting

0.7 MPa : Miscellaneous usage including air horn

control air, including the safety air and maneuvering system

Deck service

0.55MPa : Hydrophore tank charging

0.2MPa : Sea chest

Main air reservoirs and aux. air reservoir shall be charged by main air compressors and emergency air compressor.

Deck service air reservoir shall be charged by the service air compressor.

Compressed air for starting the main engine shall be supplied from the main air reservoirs. Generator engines shall be supplied from the main air reservoirs or the aux. air reservoir.

The deck service compressed air to be supplied from service air reservoir and main air reservoirs via pressure reducing valve.

The pressure reducing valve shall be provided with a pressure relief valve and a pressure gauge at its outlet and the stand-by pressure reducing valve shall be provided.

Maneuvering and control air shall be supplied through one (1) pressure reducing valve and one (1) dehydrator from the main air reservoirs.

Separate airline shall be provided for air horns with locally open valve.

Air hose connections shall be provided at suitable locations in the engine room.

### 6.11.6 STEAM AND DRAIN SYSTEM

Following system shall be provided

a) Steam supply system

b) Condense system

Steam shall be supplied to various services at following pressure:

0.7 MPa: HFO and LSHFO/ULSFO service and settling tanks heating

HFO,LSHFO/ULSFO heater for F.O. supply module unit

HFO,LSHFO/ULSFO &LO heaters for purifiers

Steam tracing

Other tank heating and heaters (in engine room)

0.4MPa: Calorifier

Air conditioning plant

Sea chests in engine room

Miscellaneous usage

Drain from HFO,ULHFO/LSHFO and lub. oil tank heating coil and oil heaters shall be led to the cascade tank through atmos. condenser and the inspection tank.

Drain from the calorifier and accommodation also shall be led to the cascade tank.

Drain traps with by-pass and check cock shall be provided for HFO,LSHFO/ULSFO and lub. Oil tank’s coil and oil heaters.

Escape lines for steam safety/relief valves shall be led to the funnel.

Flange type or screw type steam hose connections shall be provided for cleaning oil tanks, sea chest etc. in the engine room.

No shore steam connection shall be provided.

The inspection tank shall be integrated with cascade tank or separately arranged.

Excess steam from M/E exhaust gas section of the composite boiler shall be led to cascade tank through auto. steam dump and atmos. condenser.

### 6.11.7 FEED WATER SYSTEM

Condensate from atmos. condenser shall be discharged to cascade tank by gravity.

Feed water pump of the composite boiler shall draw water from the cascade tank and then discharge it to the composite boiler.

Feed water to cascade tank shall be manually from the F.W. hydrophore.

The bottom and surface blow down lines of the composite boiler shall be combined to led overboard.

The blow-down lines shall have double valves.

Each feed water pump shall have a capacity for max. evaporation when the main engine operating at SMCR and one (1) pump of them shall serve as stand-by.

### 6.11.8 SHIP'S SERVICE SYSTEM OF ENGINE ROOM

#### 6.11.8.1 Bilge System

The engine room bilge system shall be served by two (2) sets of fire, bilge & G.S. pump, one (1) set of daily bilge pump **and one (1) set of Clean Drain Tank Pump**

One (1) set of dangerous goods bilge eductor for cargo holds shall be arranged in suitable place outside engine room*,* the pump shall be used for pumping the bilge of cargo holds when carry dangerous goods.

Each bilge well in engine room shall have a suction line with mud box and a stop check valve and shall be connected to the bilge main. The daily bilge pump shall take suction from the bilge main to the bilge holding tank. The oily bilge separator pump shall take suction from the oily bilge holding tank, and discharge overboard through the oily bilge separator and separated oil shall be automatically drained to the sludge tank by gravity.

***The IBTS shall be complied.***

***Clean bilge in engine room shall be led to the clean drain tank, and discharge overboard by the Clean Drain Tank Pump. An independent 15 PPM monitor to be provided on pump discharge side.***

Bilge suction shall be provided for double bottom cofferdams in engine room and main engine recess on tank top.

In addition to the suction from bilge main suction, one of the two fire, bilge & G.S. pumps shall have an independent bilge suction from the bilge well in the engine room.

The emergency suction line with non-return stop valve shall be connected to a ballast pump or a cooling sea water pump as per the Rule requirement.

Bilge high level alarm for each bilge well in engine room and cargo holds shall be provided. ***And before the suction pipe there is a mud box installed for each well.***

In general, the valves in engine room bilge system shall be manual operation.

#### 6.11.8.2 Water Fire Fighting System

##### 6.11.8.2.1 Sea Water Fire Fighting System

The fire main shall be served by the fire, bilge & G.S. pumps and emergency fire pump (in emergency case).

The fire hydrants with manual operation and hose boxes shall be arranged on platforms.

##### 6.11.8.2.2 Water Mist Fire Fighting System

The fixed low pressure water mist local application system shall be provided in engine room to protect following fire hazard space such as main engine, generator sets, boiler, fueloil purifiers, fuel oil booster and incinerator.

The system consists of water pump unit, F.W. tank, water nozzles, pipes, alarm system and release station etc.

The system shall have both automatic release located outside of the engine room and local manual release.

***Power for system must be routed through the Emergency Generator Switch Board.***

#### 6.11.8.3 CO2 Fire Fighting System

The system refers to Hull Piping Chapter.

#### 6.11.8.4 Ballast System

Two (2) sets of ballast pump shall be used for ballasting and de-ballasting via ballast water treatment plant. Generally one pump to work, and the other to be stand-by. Ballast stripping shall be carried out by one (1) ballast stripping eductor.

The detail refers to Hull Piping Chapter.

6.11.8.5 Fresh Water System

Fresh water shall be supplied by two (2) sets of fresh water pump with one (1) set of fresh water hydrophore tank.

Fresh water shall be supplied from hydrophore tank for domestic service in living quarters, technical fresh water service and calorifier in engine room.

The engine room technical water service shall be supplied directly from the fresh water hydrophore tank.

The fresh water pump to take suction from fresh water tank through a strainer and discharge to the fresh water hydrophore tank, fitted with limit pressure switch adjusted to start and stop the fresh water pump motor within a preset pressure range.

One of two fresh water pumps shall be used as stand-by.

Fresh water to main deck shall be provided with isolating valve and drain valve located at the lowest point (accommodation face).

The hot water shall be supplied by a calorifier with steam and electric heating.

One (1) set of F.W. sterilizer and one (1) set of mineralizing shall be provided for potable fresh water system.

Y- type filter shall be arranged before the F.W. sterilizer.

For fresh water system description, also refer to Chapter 6 - Hulling Piping , 6.1.8.

#### 6.11.8.6 Sea Chests

There are one (1) high suction sea chest and one (1) low suction sea chest in engine room and one (1) suction sea chest in emergency fire pump room. Each suction sea chest shall be fitted with a sea valve of butterfly type.

Each suction sea chest shall be of welded steel construction. A steam and compressed air blow out connection and an air vent to be equipped for engine room sea chests. But only a compressed air blow out connection and an air vent to be equipped for the sea chest of emergency fire pump.

Each suction sea chest shall be equipped with grid, made of galvanized steel flat bars, with a clear area of at least two (2) times the area of the sea valves.

Grid shall be secured to the chest so that no part extends beyond the shell surface.

Fitting bolts and nuts of sea chest grids shall be of stainless steel and locked by stainless steel wire.

One (1) marine growth preventing system shall be installed in main SW strainers for main sea chests in engine room only.

### 6.11.9 EXHAUST GAS SYSTEM

Exhaust gas from the turbocharger of the main engine shall be led to the M/E exhaust gas section of the composite boiler , scrubber unit and discharged directly to open air.

No exhaust gas by-pass line to be provided for exhaust gas section of the composite boiler.

The oil fired section and incinerator shall be led up independently to open air.

Exhaust gas from G/E sets engine shall be led up independently to scrubber unit through each silencer.

Stainless steel expansion elements for exhaust gas pipes of main and gen. engines shall be fitted immediately after turbocharger through transition connection.

Adequate supports shall be fitted so that the weight of the piping shall not rest on the turbocharger, boiler, incinerator, silencers and expansion elements, etc.

***Recommend amend to Exhaust gas uptakes in the funnel to be insulated up to about at least 1,000 mm from the top plate of funnel.***

Necessary drains from the exhaust gas pipes and silencers shall be arranged with drain traps and led to bilge well.

### 6.11.10 INSTRUMENTATION

Following instrument shall be provided for each machinery or on the piping side, and exclusive of the instruments used for automatic control in ECR.

#### 6.11.10.1 Pressure, Compound and Vacuum Gauges

Pressure, compound and vacuum gauges shall be manufactured in accordance with the Chinese Industrial Standard or equivalent for marine use.

All gauge to have black figures, white faces, letter in English and units in metric or SI system (Red figures for vacuum), and working range shall be clearly marked for each gauge. Following gauges shall be furnished.

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Place of installation | No. of set | Diameter of gauge (mm) | Remark |
| Water | Centrifugal pumps suction & delivery | 1 each | 100 |  |
| Reciprocating pumps suction & delivery | 1 each |  |
| Oil | Rotary pumps suction & delivery | 1 each |  |
| Oil strainer inlet & outlet | 1 each |  |
| Steam  &  Condensate | Boiler drum | 2 | 150 |  |
| Heaters (steam side) | 1 each | 100 |  |

#### 6.11.10.2 Thermometers

Thermometers shall be indicated in Centigrade and shall be manufactured in accordance with the International Standard or equivalent, and working range shall be clearly marked for each gauge. Thermometers of liquid in glass type with separable sockets shall be provided as follows.

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Place of installation | | No. of  set | Remarks |
| Water | Fresh water cooler | Fresh water & sea water inlet & outlet | 1 each | Fresh water: after temp. control valve |
|  | Atmospheric condenser | Cooling water inlet & outlet | 1 each |  |
|  | Lub. oil cooler | Cooling water inlet & outlet | 1 each | Lub. oil: after temp. cont. valve |
| Oil | Heaters | Oil inlet & outlet | 1 each |  |
|  | Heated tanks | Oil pocket on tank wall or outlet | 1 each |  |
| Others | Various thermometers fitted at main engine, generator engines, air compressors, stern tube bearing, boiler | | Assorted |  |
|  | Oil purifiers | Acc.to Maker's standard |  |  |

## 6.12 scrubber system

The SOX Scrubber system shall be of open loop type and shall be able to treat the exhaust gas from one (1) main engine and three (3) generator engines to achieve the 0.5%S ***(Option 0.1%S)*** equivalency to meet the “Global Sulphur Cap 2020”.

The open loop system is typically used in open waters where the alkalinity of the seawater is higher than 2,200μmol/l for effective scrubbing.

The SOx scrubber system is designed to remove sulphur oxides from main engine and generator engines exhaust gases. The removal efficiency for SOx of the open loop system is from max. 3.5%S to 0.5%S. ***(Option: to achieve the 0.1%S equivalency to meet the SECA requirement)***

One(1) common scrubber unit with a combine box for ME and three(3) sets of GEs.

M.G.O. will be used as stand-by for main engine and generator engines when SOx scrubber system is fault, and when local regulations prevent or limit the use of the open loop system due to low alkalinity or restricted discharge criteria, the MGO could be used.

Boiler exhaust gas pipe will not connect to SOx scrubber system.

The open loop system uses pure sea water for neutralizing the exhaust gas. The water is taken from sea chest, pumped to the scrubber tower and distributed to the active spray nozzles. Drain is led directly via sea water overboard discharge line, the discharge criteria set by the IMO guidelines should be met (the PH should be equals or above 6.5 at a distance 4 meters from the discharge point.

The open loop SOx scrubber system capacity is based on the following operational profile:

- M/E SMCR

- Two (2) sets G/E at 85% load

***The boiler is only connect to the scrubber tower, not enlarge the scrubber system’s capacity, and the boiler is only working in port.***

The backpressure limit for M/E and G/Es will be increased as per maker’s standard, the fuel oil consumption may suffer penalty as per maker’s calculation, no exhaust gas fan is provided for M/E and G/E in principle.

Continuous emission monitoring system and water monitoring unit shall be provided, the materials, accessories and fittings will be in accordance with Maker’s standard and requirement of Classification Society.

***The discharge pipes to be GRE and the last connection to the ship side should be duplex S32750***

## 6.13 SPARE PARTS AND TOOLS

All spare parts and special tools shall be supplied according to the Rules of Classification Society and manufacturer’s standard.

***Normally only 1 set spare for each type equipment, such as Aux engines, just one set spare for three Aux engines.***

***The spares list will be supplied to the owner after the yard receive the approved drawing from maker. The list will be checked by yard, if have any deviation, the shipyard will inform the owner.***

General tools and outfits for machinery part are supplied according to builder standard.

# CHAPTER 7 AUTOMATION AND REMOTE CONTROL

## **7.1** General

## **7.1.1** Principle

Automatic control, remote operation, instrumentation and central supervision shall be so designed and arranged that the propulsion plant is capable of being operated for 24 hours under normal sea-going condition without manual attendance in engine room to comply with the requirement for the ship with Classification notation (refer to Chapter 1 General 1.3.1).

One (1) control room shall be arranged in the engine room, where the control console of main engine and the main switchboard shall be installed.

The instrument gauge and alarm shall be arranged in good order for safety operation and easy maintenance.

Automatic combustion control and equipment concerned with the boiler shall be arranged adjacent to the boiler.

Automatic controllers and control valves shall be provided on principal systems for safety operation and easy maintenance.

The entire automation system shall consist of several decentralized control systems.

The decentralized control systems shall be used separately for main engine remote control, power management control, stand-by pump changeover control, and engine room monitoring and alarm system, ballast and bilge system.

The machinery and equipment not specified in this specification shall be served locally by the engine personnel on site, according to needs.

In case that the contents in the following parts of this section differ from Maker’s standard for specific equipment, Makers’ standard shall be applied in general.

**UPS for AMS are to be provided. Duration of the batteries shall be minimum 30 min and tested during sea trials.**

**Serial and analog signals to AMS are to be isolated in equipment / device / sensor side as maker’s standard. Digital signals are to be voltage free contact signals.**

## **7.1.2** Control standS

The following control stands shall be provided:

- Wheelhouse control console (WHC) including Bridge Maneuvering Console (BMC) and Navigation Signal Console (NSC) in wheelhouse

- Engine control room console (ECC) in engine control room.

- Ballast control station in ship office.

- Local stands for local controls of machines.

- Bridge wing control console at navigation bridge deck wings.

1. Bridge maneuvering console

Refer to “Chapter 8 Electric”.

2. Engine control room console

The console shall be of steel construction self-standing type, with hinged doors in front side and removable doors in rear side if applicable.

The console shall be supplied from main switchboard and emergency switchboard by means of each one feeder 3 x 220V AC, and from charging & discharging board by means of one feeder 24V DC.

Inside the console AC220 V socket outlets shall be provided.

Inside the console 2 pcs of AC220V 20W lights should be provided.

The following equipment shall be included in/on the console, but not limit to:

*-* Main propulsion–main operation panel / safety panel

- Main engine indication panel

- Engine telegraph (receiver / transmitter)

- 2 pcs of PC workstation with 24 inch TFT VDU and other engine room monitoring and alarm equipment

- Alarm & Data logging printer

- Slave clock

- Dead man alarm main switch or push button (combined in extension alarm panel)

- Remote water level analogue or digital indicator for boiler

- Main engine auxiliary blower, and start / stop switch with running indication lampas per main engine Maker’s standard

- Composite boiler emergency stop push button

- Composite boiler running (firing on) lamp

- Composite boiler steam pressure gauge

- Main engine RPM indicator and revolution counter

- Main engine turbocharger RPM indicator

* Scrubber monitoring and shut-down control in emergency

- Rudder angle indicator

- Analogue measuring instruments for essential pressures and temperatures

- Main air compressor auto/start/stop switch and running indication

- Fuel oil viscosity indication

- HFO, LSHFO and MGO change-over position indicator

- Duty engineer selector

- Auto. telephone

- Speed log indicator

- Sound power telephone

- Suitable place for writing

- Lubricator controller .

- Temperature controllers of HT, LT & LO.

- M/E running hour counter

Water mist alarm repeater panel

Manual emergency trip buttons with cover of necessary

- Other necessary equipment specified elsewhere

3. Ballast control station in ship office. Refer to item 1-14.

4. Local stand for local control of main engine. Refer to “Chapter 6 Machinery”.

5. Bridge wing console at navigation bridge deck wing. Refer to “Chapter 8 – Electric”.

## **7.1.3** Control room

1. Engine control room (ECR)

Engine control room surrounded with steel walls shall be sound insulated and air conditioned.

In the ECR the following equipment shall be provided:

- Main switchboard

* Engine control console; One monitor for Valve remote control system along with tank level remote gauge shall be combined.

- Uninterrupted Power Supply unit for automation system (UPS)

* Auto telephone and sound power telephone

- Electronic modules and operator panels for M/E remote control system

- ECR manual control panel of M/E

- Fire alarm repeater panel

- Air condition unit

- Remote valve operation and tank sounding shall be possible from ECR and ship office.

- Other necessary furniture specified elsewhere

2. Ship office

In the ship office the following equipment shall be provided:

- Ballast control station

- Auto. telephone

- AMS Extend alarm panel

- Reefer container monitoring panel

- Loading computer

* 1 pcs of 24 inch TFT VDU for ballast control and level measure system
* Anti-heeling system control
* Ballast water treatment system panel
* Cargo hold fans remote control and running indicator

## **7.2** Automation System

## **7.2.1** Engine’s Alarm and Monitoring System

The micro-processor aided integrated alarm and monitoring system (AMS) to be provided.

The system consists of the following equipment:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Equipment | QTY. | Location |
| PC workstation with24 inch TFT VDU | 2 | ECC |
| PC workstation with24 inch TFT VDU | 1 | WHC  ( for monitoring ) |
| Alarm printer &Data logging printer | 1 | ECC |
| Extension alarm panel | 11 | Accommodation |
| Alarm lamp | \* | ECC |
| UPS | \* | ECC |

Comments: AT with mark “\*”is specified hereinafter.

The system shall be based on a concept of totally distributed processing which various processes are controlled by input/output modules located near equipment. Ample hardwired I/O and serial I/O shall be provided as per Rule and Maker’s standard.

The system shall have the following functions:

* Data processing function
* Data storage function
* Data indicating function
* Alarm function
* Data logging function
* Alarm logging function
* Extension alarm function

1. Main parts of Engine’s alarm and monitoring system (AMS) shall have redundant functionality, the system shall be based on computer with alarm, and monitoring signals connected to I/O units arranged in the engine room and in the control room or other spaces.

2. All input channels shall be made in “self-check-off” principle

3. The particular measured analogue data shall be continuously indicated on individual analogue indicator.

4. Alarm shall be initiated when measured analogue data exceeds corresponding alarm preset analogue value as well as deviations from the mean value for the main engine exhaust gas.

5. Common sound alarm in ECR with flashing light or indication in each particular channel shall signalize the alarm conditions. After acceptance the failure condition, the flashing light or indication signal shall be turned to steady one and sound signal shall be silenced.

The steady light shall be automatically cancelled after normal condition has been restored and the alarm signal has been acknowledged.

When the arrangement is stopped intentionally, the respective alarm circuits shall be switched off automatically.

6. Each alarm condition shall be transmitted to the E/R alarm column system in ECR and engine room as well as to extension alarm system panels.

7. The failure alarms shall be divided at least in the following groups:

a. “Trip” group: alarms signaling faults, which require the propulsion system, shall be shut down immediately.

b. “Reduce” group: alarms signaling faults, which require a power reduction in the propulsion system.

c. “Common” group: alarms signaling faults which do not require actions as described in a or b.

d. Individual alarm: The alarm shall be individual transmitted to extension alarm system, including the engine room fire, bilge level high, system power source fault etc.

8. Extension alarm system panels with sound and light signals, installed in

- Wheelhouse

- Chief engineer's day room (with additional buzzer in bed room)

- 2nd, 3rd, 4th Engineer’s cabin

- Engineer’s office

- Officer’s mess room

- Recreation room

- Gymnasium

- Ship office

- Electrician’s cabin

The extension alarm system panels shall be able to indicate different alarm groups.

9. Engine room “Dead man” alarm

The system shall be switched-on in activating boxes at two main ER entrances and shall be reset within preset time by reset push-buttons with indication lamp, situated in:

- engine control room

- engine room (6 pcs)

10. Power supply arrangement

The entire system with operator stations I/O units shall be powered from 24V DC.

Note: The alarm and monitoring system (AMS) to be in accordance with rule requirement and may be changed according to final selected Maker’s standard.

## **7.2.2** Automation System

All pneumatic valves / items for main engine control should be tagged by stainless steel name plate with valve position deeply etched on it. This should exactly match with control drawing.

Automation system consists of the following subsystems:

1. DG Power Management System Refer to item 1-5.

2. Automatic change-over of stand-by pumps

The following pumps to be automatically changed-over by low pressure or low level and abnormal trip:

- Cooling S.W. pump

- M/E jacket cooling F.W. pump

- L.T. cooling F.W. pump

- Composite boiler feed water pump

- F.O. pumps attached to the F.O. supply module unit

- Composite boiler F.O. supply pump

- Main L.O. pump

3. Automatic regulation of temperature and viscosity

The following equipment and systems to be provided with automatic regulation of temperature or/and viscosity.

- HFO/LSHFO settling and service tanks (refer to Chapter 6 Machinery 6. 2.17)

- Oil purifier’s heater (acc. to Maker’s recommendation)

- F.O. supply module unit (acc. to Maker’s recommendation)

- Generator engines (acc. to Maker’s recommendation)

- Calorifier

- M/E and G/E pre-heaters (acc. to Maker’s recommendation)

- Following ancillary system for main engine (if necessary)

M/E jacket cooling F.W. circuit

Central F.W. coolers outlet

M/E L.O. cooler outlet

4. Ballast/bilge/fuel oil transfer pumps and valves/control system

Refer to item 1-14.

5. Automatic start and stop

HFO/*LSHFO/*ULSFO transfer pump

## **7.2.3** Main Propulsion Control

Main propulsion control shall consist of main engine control system, safety device and engine telegraph system, ***Telegraph logger to be connected to master clock***.

## **7.2.3.1** Main Engine Control System

***A circuit breakers as protective device shall be prepared for the control circuits in the switchboards.***

1. Local control

Manual, emergency controls from M/E local operating panel placed on the engine in engine room with following functions:

Start/stop, reversing, speed control, and the most important engine data displayed.

2. Remote control from engine control room

Main operating panel shall be used for carrying out engine commands, adjust the engine parameters, select the running modes, and observe the status of the control system.

3. Remote control from wheelhouse or navigation bridge deck wings

The following controls shall be sequentially performed according to a preset RPM time loading program by operating the engine telegraph in wheelhouse or navigation bridge deck wings:

Starting and stopping

Speed increasing and decreasing as per engine design

Reversing

The reversing and speed setting of M/E shall be controlled by engine telegraph lever which is used as maneuvering lever.

Main engine speed control shall be carried out through the electronic speed control system.

In case of the first starting failure, two or more staring attempts shall be automatically carried out (total three attempts). An alarm shall be given after three attempts without firing. Re-starting shall be carried out after setting the telegraph lever at the “STOP” position.

The auxiliary blower shall be automatically started and stopped by detecting the scavenging air manifold pressure, and also shall be capable of being started and stopped from engine control room.

4. Control position transfer system

Engine running modes shall be done from the main operating panel in ECR.

Control shall be done from one station only at a time.

(1) Local – engine control room

Maneuvering position change-over between the engine side and the engine control room shall be carried out at the engine side.

(2) Engine control room – wheelhouse

Maneuvering position change-over between the wheelhouse and the engine control room shall be carried out in the engine control room.

(3) Wheelhouse – navigation bridge deck wings

Maneuvering position change-over between the wheelhouse and the both bridge wings shall be carried out in the wheelhouse.

## **7.2.3.2** Protecting and safety devices

a. Emergency trip

Main engine shall be automatically tripped with an alarm according to Rules and propulsion plant manufacturer's requirements.

Each one manual emergency trip push button with cover shall be provided in engine control console, local emergency control station, navigation bridge deck wings and W/H control console.

Emergency trip system shall be independent of the remote control system and separated from Engine’s alarm and monitoring system.

Reset of trip circuit shall be carried out by setting the maneuvering/telegraph lever in engine control room at stop position after recovering to normal condition.

b. Critical speed protection

Automatic quick passing program shall be applied over the critical revolution zone during bridge control (if any).

Critical speed alarm to be provided in AMS ***for the long time running***.

c. Program speed control

When controlled in wheelhouse, the engine speed shall be controlled by load-up / load down program over certain ahead speed by program device with readjusted time up to the set speed of the maneuvering / telegraph lever.

One override push button for program speed up shall be provided in each of wheelhouse control console and navigation bridge deck wings.

d. Turning interlock

While the turning gear is engaged, a starting pilot air valve for starting shall be locked.

e. Automatic slow-down

The M/E speed shall be automatically reduced according to Rules and propulsion plant Manufacturer's requirements.

One by-pass push button of this system shall be provided in each of W/H control console and navigation bridge deck wings or as per maker standard.

Reset of the automatic slow down circuit shall be carried out by setting the telegraph lever in selected main engine control position below a predetermined position after recovering to normal condition.

Alarm and separate indicator for above as well as emergency trip shall be provided on engine control console in engine control room and W/H control console.

## **7.2.3.3** Telegraph System

Telegraph system shall consist of engine telegraph, sub-engine telegraph and telegraph logger.

1. Engine telegraph

One (1) set of engine order telegraph system shall be provided, and it is to consist of:

1 - transmitter with receiver with buzzer and illuminating lamp and dimmer in wheelhouse control console

1 – transmitter (remote control lever) with buzzer and illuminating lamp and dimmer in each of navigation bridge deck wings

1 – receiver / reply with bell in engine control console

1 – receiver / with gong in engine side

During wheelhouse control or navigation bridge deck wing control of main engine, the buzzer shall sound for abt. 2 seconds when the order partition is changed.

2. Sub-engine telegraph

One (1) set of sub-engine telegraph of push button with lamp type shall be provided in wheelhouse and engine control room.

Partitions of the sub-telegraph shall be as follows:

AT SEA

STAND-BY

FINISHED WITH ENGINE

Audible devices of the sub-engine telegraph shall be one buzzer in each of wheelhouse and engine control room.

3. Telegraph logger

One (1) telegraph logger shall be provided in wheelhouse. The following items shall be recorded:

Engine telegraph order & reply

Sub-engine telegraph order & reply

Time

The recorded time shall be synchronous with Master clock.

The achieved revolutions and time corresponding to the revolution

Note: The M/E remote control system and telegraph system to be in accordance with rule requirement and may be changed according to final selected Maker’s standard.

## **7.2.3.4** Shafting Revolution Indicators

One (1) set of shafting revolution-indicating system shall be provided and installed at

following places.

One (1) pick-up type transmitter on M/E flywheel.

One (1) flush type RPM indicator with an illumination on wheelhouse ceiling console with

separate dimmer switch on W/H control console.

Each wall type RPM indicator (with dimmer) on each bridge wings.

One (1) flush type RPM indicator on the engine control console and Chief Engineer’s day

room.

One (1) electric or mechanical type indicator at main engine machine side according to

engine Maker's standard.

One (1) shaft revolution counter of 8digits shall be provided on engine control console.

## **7.2.4** Control of electric gneeratring plant

## **7.2.4.1** Main generator sets

The main generator sets shall be either manually remote controlled or automatically control, and also be capable of being started and stopped locally. Three(3) engine generators shall be capable of being set in stand-by with the selecting switch on main switchboard.

1. Manual control

The generator's engines shall be provided with remote manual starting and stopping facilities, EMCY stop and speed control switch in MSB, and local start/stop shall be also provided.

Manual synchronizing shall be available by means of synchronoscope and synchronizing lamps and the governor control switches for diesel generators on main switchboard.

Manual load sharing shall be carried out with the governor control switches for generators on main switchboard.

1. Automatic control

The main generating plant shall be automatically controlled by means of Power Management System (PMS) and safety system i.e.

- Automatic start/stop

- Monitoring of critical parameters

- Safety system with shutdown

- Automatic synchronizing

- Automatic load sharing

- Frequency control

- Load dependent start / stop

- Bow thruster start inquiry

1) Automatic start and stop of stand-by generator

When loading of a running generator is over about 90% of rated load, the predetermined generator shall be started, synchronized and the circuit breaker of started generator shall be closed and the load shall be shared automatically.

When two (2) or more generators are running in parallel and the total power is below about certain percentage of one generator’s rated load, the predetermined generator in running shall shift the load and the circuit breaker shall be opened and the engine shall be stopped after a time delay automatically.

Stand-by generator shall be automatically started in the following conditions:

(1) Power failure of main bus

(2) Low frequency of main bus

(3) Low voltage of main bus

(4) High voltage of main bus

(5) Trip of any air circuit breaker of running generators

(6) Over load (when one generator is running)

2) In case of above items (1) to (4)

The circuit breaker of running generator shall be automatically opened, and the circuit breaker of started generator shall be closed.

Then, some essential electric equipment formerly operated shall be automatically connected in sequence.

3) In case of above items (5) and (6)

The started generator shall be automatically synchronized and connected to main bus, and then the loads of generators shall be automatically shared.

The stand-by set shall be pre-lubricated according to Maker’s requirement. Automatic/manual selecting switch for pre-lubricating pump of each set shall be arranged in the starter.

When main generators operate in parallel and one of them fails, the preference trip system to be initiated and trip the non-essential loadsinclude Bow thruster. The non-essential consumers shall be manually restarted after tripping.

In case of “black-out”, the stand-by set shall be started automatically.

*Interlock between PMS operation and Generator standby system to be provided to prevent PMS selection when no generator is put on standby*.

## **7.2.4.2** Emergency diesel generator set

The emergency generator set shall be automatically started, the bus tie breaker in emergency switchboard shall be automatically opened, and the air circuit breaker shall be automatically closed in case of failure in supply feeder from main switchboard.

And then, when electric source on main bus is recovered, the air circuit breaker shall be automatically opened and the engine shall be stopped after a time delay automatically, and the bus tie breaker shall be automatically closed.

Manual start and stop of the generator set shall be carried out on site.

The automatic and manual control system shall be according to the Maker’s standard.

## **7.2.5** Composite Boiler

1. Automatic combustion control

The fuel oil burning set for oil fired section of the composite boiler shall be provided with electric modulating controlling system.

The burner shall be automatically lit and extinguished according to the boiler steam pressure.

The burner shall be turned off automatically according to the rules. The manual stopping device shall be provided in ECC.

2. Automatic control of surplus steam

When the steam pressure generated by M/E exhaust gas section of the composite boiler is over the predetermined limit, the surplus steam shall be led to the atmospheric condenser automatically through a surplus steam dump valve.

3. Automatic control of boiler water level

Water level of the boiler shall be regulated automatically by level switch on the boiler.

4. Alarm and protection

The alarm signals for pressure, temperature and combustion shall be connected to alarm and monitoring system (AMS) in compliance with the Rules and Maker’s standard.

## **7.2.6** Control of Oil Purifiers

All purifiers shall be manually ON/OFF control on site operation and cleaning process –fully automated.

Alarm and recirculation of oil feed to purifier upon loss of seal shall be provided for the purifier according to Maker's standard. Feed oil will be re-circulated by three way shifting valve, as per Maker’s standard.

All oil purifiers shall be designed to have manual emergency stop function***, the emergency stop button shall be locate at the suitable place by the designing.***

Running indication shall be in ECC. Alarm shall be in alarm and monitoring system (AMS). Auto. sludge discharging shall be performed.

Hour counter for each purifier shall be provided or displayed in control board.

## **7.2.7** Control of Air Compressors

1. Starting of main air compressors

The starting of main air compressors shall be automatically ON/OFF controlled, depending on pressure of common inlet pipe of the main air reservoirs in the following sequence:

- At abt. 2.8 MPa – start the first leading main air compressor

- At abt. 2.6 MPa – start the second leading main air compressor (operating both compressors)

- All compressors stop at 3.0 MPa

Any compressor can be selected as first leading, second leading.

The main air compressor shall be automatically started and stopped by detecting the pressure of common inlet pipe of main air reservoirs. The relocation of start/stop setting points shall be possible.

A common failure alarm for automatic tripping shall be sent to alarm and monitoring system (AMS). Safety installation for the compressors shall be provided in accordance with the maker's recommendation.

Hour counter of each compressor shall be provided in control board.

A remote control for the main air compressors shall be arranged.

Main air compressor auto/start/stop switch and running indication to be provided in ECC

2. Control air treatment station

Control air installation shall be supplied from air treatment station with pressure 0.8MPa

The air treatment station shall be supplied from main air reservoir by means of reduction valve 3.0 / 0.8 MPa and consists of:

- Air dehydrator

- Reduction valve and safety valve

- Pressure gauge at each pressure output

## **7.2.8** Scrubber Operation and Control

The operation and control system shall be the type of programmable logic controller (PLC) Following parameters shall be continuously monitoring for the cleaned exhaust gas and water emissions:

* Wash water turbidity, pH value, etc. of outlet;
* CO2/SO2 analysis measuring for exhaust gas outlet
* ME/AE power signal and GPS signal shall be supplied by Yard for logging
* etc.

An operating station shall be in the ECC for the system operation.

## **7.2.9** Special Control Functions

The important equipment, if formerly operated, shall be automatically, sequentially restarted when electric power on main bus is recovered after “black-out”.

## **7.2.10** Local Automatic Control

The following auxiliaries to be operated in local automatic system:

* Fresh water generator abnormal alarm shall be connected to AMS and high salinity alarm in monitoring system.
* Salinometer shall be provided with automatic control to re-circulate distillate on high salinity.
* F. W. pumps shall be automatically operated in dependence on the tanks pressure
* Oily bilge separator with failure/15ppm alarm in alarm and monitoring system (AMS).
* Incinerator with failure alarm in alarm and monitoring system (AMS).
* Sewage treatment plant with failure alarm in alarm and monitoring system (AMS).
* Ballast water treatment plant with failure alarm in alarm and monitoring system and remote control from ships office.

## **7.2.11** Miscellaneous Controls

1. Start/stop control of fire, bilge & G.S. pump in W/H control console and machine side and in fire control station also.
2. Engine room ventilation fans – start / stop control in MSB.
3. START / STOP control of sludge pump.
4. Engine room bilge pumps and valves – locally controlled.
5. Remote emergency stop.
6. Remote start-stop switches and running indicating lamps for cargo hold ventilating fans shall be installed in wheel house ***along with one common isolation switch (key type) to isolate non-Ex. Proof vent fans during dangerous cargo loading through the AMS mimic diagram.***.

Emergency stop push button shall be arranged near shore discharge station for sludge pump and bilge pump.

Ventilating fans and oil pumps shall be stopped in an emergency case of fire.

- Ventilating fans in engine room, fuel and lub. oil pumps, boiler, purifiers, incinerator in engine room shall be remote stopped. Emergency stop push-buttons shall be provided in fire control station, wheelhouse and entrance of engine room.

- Separate emergency stop push-buttons of ventilation fans for accommodation and ventilation fans for cargo hold shall be installed in wheelhouse and fire control station.

- Boiler plant and incinerator can be emergency stopped in engine control room. In addition, Boiler Running, boiler water levels and steam pressure indications are to be provided in the ECR console

***Builder shall prepare a list to Buyer for the memory batteries of individual equipment control circuit, which shall including the reference data of type and replacement dates etc. that necessary for the batteries replacement work.***

## **7.2.12** Running Lamps

As a Rule, machinery controlled from MSB or ECC shall be equipped with running lamps there.

## **7.2.13** Remote Quick Closing Valve

Quick closing facilities for pneumatic remote closing valves in fuel oil and lub. oil systems shall be provided.

Low pressure alarm shall be provided to AMS.

## **7.2.14** Ballast Control Station

Entire system shall be based one (1) pc of PC workstation with 24 inch TFT in engine control room, one (1) pc of PC workstation in ship office.

The following system shall be provided in above monitor:

- Ballast control system

- Fuel oil filling control system (only indication)

- Valves remote control system

- Level and draught gauging system

- Bilge control system.

All measured data in level and draught gauging system shall be transmitted to loading computer via interface.

1. Ballast system

Display of mimic diagram of the following:

- Valve control for remote control valves and open/shut indication

- Start/stop control for ballast pumps

- Running indication for ballast pumps

- Tank level and content display (water ballast tanks and fresh water tanks)

- Ship's draught display

2. Fuel oil filling control system

The fuel oil filling system shall be remote controlled from engine control room as follows:

- Remote control of HFO/LSHFO transfer pump

- Running indication for HFO/LSHFOtransfer pump and MDO/MGO transfer pump

- Remote control valves in fuel oil filling system and open/shut indication

- Remote level measurement in fuel oil tanks and alarm of overflow and filling up

Start / stop push buttons shall be installed near the HFO/LSHFO transfer pump, MDO/MGO transfer pump separately.

Stop push-button for HFO/LSHFOtransfer pump in bunker station to be provided. The auto start/stop shall be applied to HFO/LSHFO settling tank by high/low level switches.

3. Valves remote control system

The valve remote control system shall be of pneumatic type.

The valve relay cabinet(s) shall be installed in engine room and cargo hold.

All remotely controlled valves shall have an emergency operation facility.

4. Level and draught gauging system

The system shall consist of electronic pressure transmitter type.

Installation of tank remote level measuring able to display tank volumes shall be provided in:

- F.O. tanks and L.O. tank in E/R (refer to part VII-Machinery, paragraph 2-17)

- Ballast tanks

- F.W. tanks

5. Bilge control system

The bilge control system shall ensure:

- Opening and closing of bilge system valves outside the engine room

- Alarm in the bilge wells of cargo hold when filled up

6. Anti-heeling system

One (1) set of separated anti heeling system shall be provided; the common alarm shall be connected to AMS.

The anti-heeling system includes as follows:

* Anti-heeling pump
* Heeling sensor and control unit in ship office
* Anti-heeling control valves

Control functions and indications shall be provided as bellows:

* Start/Stop function for automatically heel adjusting
* Start/Stop function with running indication for heeling pump
* Lower level alarm and stop for heeling pump
